Permissibility of Using Rebel Weapons in Battle
Ruling statement on using rebel weapons in battle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using rebel weapons in battle and identify the condition that permits it.

Core Idea
Rebel weapons may be used against them only when needed — necessity permits what is normally prohibited.

This lesson presents a concise ruling from the Hanafi matn regarding a specific battlefield situation: the use of weapons captured from rebels. While rebel property is generally protected, necessity in combat creates an exception. Understanding this conditional permission is crucial for applying fiqh in military contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Determine what action is being ruled upon: using rebel weapons to fight against them.
The act is 'yuqatilu bi silahihim' – fighting with their weapons.
2
Identify the Ruling
The ruling is 'la ba'sa' – no harm, meaning it is permissible. Note the permissibility level.
The phrase indicates permissibility, not obligation.
3
Identify the Condition
The permission is conditional on 'in ihtaju al-muslimun ilayhi' – if the Muslims need them. This restricts the ruling.
Without need, the general prohibition on taking rebel property applies.
4
Understand the Exception
Recognize that this is an exception to the general rule that rebel property is inviolable. The underlying principle is necessity (darurah).
The exception is limited to weapons and to the duration of need.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بان يقاتلوا بسلاحهم ان احتاج المسلمون اليه.
And there is no harm if they fight with their weapons if the Muslims need them.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement from the matn. It permits the use of weapons taken from rebels (presumably in battle) by Muslim forces against them, provided there is a genuine need. The ruling implies that although the property of rebels is generally protected and not ghanimah, in the heat of battle, their weapons can be used as a necessity. This is an exception to the general rule that rebel property is not to be taken. The condition is 'if the Muslims need them', indicating that it is not a general permission for plunder but a practical allowance for combat effectiveness.

Key Terms
سلاح (silaah): Weapons, arms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is it permissible for Muslims to use weapons taken from rebels?
A) Always, since they are rebels
B) Only if the Muslims need them
C) Only after the battle is over
D) Only with the permission of the rebel leader

Key Takeaway
Rebel weapons may be used against them only when needed; necessity permits what is normally prohibited.

Silk Ruling and the Leaning on Silk Dispute
Ruling with proof on silk prohibition and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on silk for men and women, identify the evidence, and distinguish between wearing and leaning on silk based on the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Silk is haram for men, halal for women; leaning on silk cushions is permissible per Abu Hanifah, makruh per Sahibayn.

This passage from Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah establishes the foundational ruling on silk. It clarifies the prohibition for men and permissibility for women, citing multiple hadith. Additionally, it addresses a practical difference within the Hanafi school: whether a man may lean on a silk cushion. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the ruling correctly in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under consideration? Wearing silk. What is the ruling? Haram for men, halal for women. Also, leaning on silk cushions is considered separately.
The passage opens the book on prohibition and permissibility.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites three hadith: Hudhayfah (forbidding silk and sitting on it), Ali (dividing a silk garment among women showing permissibility for women), and Ali (silk and gold haram for males). Identify the source and content.
All hadith are from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each hadith prove the ruling? The explicit prohibition (نهى) indicates haram for men. The action of Ali dividing the garment shows permissibility for women. The explicit statement 'haram on the males of my ummah' is clear.
The reasoning is direct from the text.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Leaning on a silk cushion: Abu Hanifah says no harm, Sahibayn say makruh. What is the basis? Abu Hanifah relies on the athar of Ibn Abbas leaning on a silk cushion. The Sahibayn may draw analogy to wearing.
This is a subsidiary issue within the school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author prefers Abu Hanifah's view, citing the athar and stating 'there is no harm'. Determine the mufta bihi and why.
The weight of a Companion's action is given priority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحظر والاباحة
[ ٣١٠١ (١) لا يحل للرجال لبس الحوير ويحل للنساء [ ۳۱۰۲ (۲) ولا بأس بتو شده
كتاب الحضر والاباحة )
ضروری نوٹ نظر کے معنی روکنا اور اباحتہ کے معنی مباح ۔ اس کتاب میں بیان کیا جائے گا کہ کون سا کام ممنوع ہے اور کون سا کام مباح ہے۔ [۳۱۰۱] (۱) مرد کے لئے ریشم کا پہننا حرام ہے اور عورت کے لئے حلال ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ عن حذيفة قال نهانا النبي الله الله ان نشرب في آنية الذهب والفضة وان ناكل فيها وعن لبس الحرير والديباج وان نجلس عليه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب افتراش الحریر، ص ۸۶۸، نمبر ۵۸۳۷ / مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم استعمال اناء الذهب والفضة على الرجال والنساء وخاتم الذهب والحرير على الرجال وا باحته للنساء ، ج ۲، ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۲۴۰۰/۲۰۶۷ / ابو داؤد
شریف ، باب ما جاء في لبس الحریر، ج ۲، ص ۲۰۴ نمبر ۴۰۴۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مردوں کے لئے ریشم کا پہننا حرام ہے۔ عورتوں کے لئے ریشم حلال ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علی بن ابی طالب قال كساني النبي له حلة سيراء فخرجت فيها فرأيت الغضب في وجهه فشققتها بين نسانی (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الحرير للنساء، ص ۸۶۸، نمبر ۱۵۸۴۰ مسلم شریف، باب تحریم لبس الحرير وغير ذلك للرجال، ج ۲، ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۲۰۶۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورتوں کے لئے ریشم حلال ہے (۲) ابوداؤد میں ہے۔ انه سمع علی بن ابی طالب يقول ان نبي الله اخذ حريرا فجعله في يمينه واخذ ذهبا فجعله في شماله ثم قال ان هذين حرام على ذكور امتی (ج) ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب في الحرير للنساء ص ۲۰۶، نمبر ۴۰۵۷) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مرد کے لئے حرام ہے لیکن عورت کے لئے جائز ہے۔
[۳۱۰۲)] (۲) اور کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس پر تکیہ لگانے میں، اور صاحبین کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے ٹیک لگانا۔ ریشم کے ستکئے پر ٹیک لگانے میں امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ نصب الرایہ میں اثر نقل کیا ہے۔ حدثنا عمرو بن ابى المقدام عن مؤذن بنى دواعة قال دخلت على ابن عباس وهو متكنى على مرفقة حرير وسعيد بن جبير عند رجليه (د) (نصب الرایة ، ج پانی ، ص ۲۸۳ را علاء السنن ، باب الا ت کا علی مرفقه الحرير للرجال، ج سابع عشر، ص ۱۳۸۰، نمبر ۵۶۶۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ریشم کے تکئے پر ٹیک لگانے میں مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حذیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مجھے حضور نے منع فرمایا کہ میں سونے اور چاندی کے برتن میں پانی پیوں اور اس میں کھانا کھاؤں، اور ریشم اور دیباج کے پہنے سے اور اس پر بیٹھنے سے منع فرمایا (ب) حضرت علی فرماتے ہیں کہ مجھے حضور نے ریشم کا صلہ دیا۔ میں اس کو پہن کر نکلا تو آپ کے چہرے پر غصے کے آثار نظر آئے تو اس کو پھاڑ کر عورتوں کے درمیان تقسیم کر دیا (ج) حضرت علی فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور نے ریشم اپنے دائیں ہاتھ میں لیا اور سونا اپنے بائیں ہاتھ میں لیا پھر فرمایا یہ دونوں میری امت کے مذکر پر حرام ہیں (1) مؤذن بنی دواعہ کہتے ہیں کہ میں حضرت ابن عباس کے پاس آیا وہ ریشم کے تکئے پر ٹیک لگائے ہوئے تھے اور سعید بن جبیر ان کے پاؤں کے پاس موجود تھے۔
Book of Prohibition and Permissibility
[3101] (1) It is not permissible for men to wear silk, and it is permissible for women. [3102] (2) And there is no harm in leaning on it.
Necessary Note: 'Hazr' means prohibition and 'Ibahah' means permissibility. In this book, it will be stated which act is prohibited and which is permissible. [3101] (1) For men, wearing silk is forbidden, and for women it is permissible.
In a hadith: From Hudhayfah, he said: 'The Prophet ﷺ forbade us from drinking in vessels of gold and silver, and from eating in them, and from wearing silk and brocade, and from sitting on them.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud) From this hadith, it is known that wearing silk is forbidden for men. Silk is permissible for women; its proof is this hadith: From Ali ibn Abi Talib, he said: 'The Prophet ﷺ gave me a silk garment. I went out wearing it, and I saw anger on his face, so I tore it and divided it among my women.' (Bukhari, Muslim) From this hadith, it is known that silk is permissible for women. (2) In Abu Dawud: He heard Ali ibn Abi Talib say: 'The Prophet of Allah ﷺ took silk in his right hand and took gold in his left hand, then said: These two are forbidden for the males of my ummah.' (Abu Dawud) From this hadith also, it is known that it is forbidden for men but permissible for women.
[3102] (2) And there is no harm in leaning on it according to Imam Abu Hanifah, and according to the Sahibayn, leaning on it is makruh. Leaning on a silk cushion according to Imam Abu Hanifah is not objectionable. In Nasb al-Rayah, an athar is transmitted: 'Amr ibn Abi al-Miqdam narrated from Mu'adhdhin of Banu Du'ah, he said: I came to Ibn Abbas while he was leaning on a silk cushion, and Sa'id ibn Jubayr was at his feet.' (Nasb al-Rayah) From this athar, it is known that there is no harm in leaning on a silk cushion.
Footnotes: (a) Hudhayfah said: The Prophet ﷺ forbade us from drinking in vessels of gold and silver, from eating in them, from wearing silk and brocade, and from sitting on them. (b) Ali said: The Prophet ﷺ gave me a silk garment... etc. (c) Ali said: The Prophet ﷺ took silk in his right hand... etc. (d) Mu'adhdhin of Banu Du'ah said: I saw Ibn Abbas leaning on a silk cushion... etc.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah, defining its scope: prohibition and permissibility. The first ruling (3101) states that silk is haram for men and halal for women. Multiple hadith support this: the Prophet forbade men from wearing silk (and from using gold/silver vessels), and when Ali wore a silk garment, the Prophet’s displeasure indicated its prohibition for men. Another hadith explicitly declares silk and gold haram for the males of his ummah. For women, the hadith where Ali divides the silk garment among women after the Prophet’s reaction shows its permissibility for them. The second ruling (3102) addresses leaning on silk cushions. Imam Abu Hanifah permits it, considering the act of leaning equivalent to using it as a furnishing, which is not specifically prohibited. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it makruh (disliked), possibly drawing analogy to wearing. The author supports Abu Hanifah’s view with a reported action of Ibn Abbas, who leaned on a silk cushion, indicating it was practiced among the Companions. The footnote summarizes the hadith sources.

Key Terms
حرير (ḥarīr): Silk fabric; the passage discusses its use in clothing and cushions.
حظر (ḥaẓr): Prohibition; the name of the book dealing with prohibited and permitted acts.
إباحة (ibāḥah): Permissibility; the opposite of prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifah regarding a man leaning on a silk cushion?
A) It is haram.
B) It is makruh.
C) There is no harm in it (ja'iz).
D) It is sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Silk is haram for men, halal for women; leaning on silk is permissible per Abu Hanifah, but makruh per Sahibayn, with the preferred view being permission.

Ruling on Silk: Haram for Men, Halal for Women
Opening of Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah with ruling on silk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on silk garments for men and women and identify the key hadith proofs that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
Wearing pure silk is haram for men and halal for women – a clear distinction based on prophetic texts.

This lesson begins the Book of Prohibition and Permission (Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah) by establishing a foundational ruling: silk is forbidden for men but permitted for women. The author presents multiple hadiths that directly address this issue, demonstrating how the Hanafi school derives its position from explicit prophetic statements. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the proofs and the reasoning behind the gender distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the opening statement that silk is not permissible for men but permissible for women. Note the terms 'hazr' and 'ibahah' as the framework.
2
Examine the first hadith proof
Read the hadith of Hudhayfah where the Prophet forbade silk along with gold and silver vessels. Understand that this is a general prohibition for men.
The hadith is from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
3
Examine the second hadith proof
Read the hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib where the Prophet gave him a silk garment, showed anger, and Ali tore it for women. This shows the permissibility for women.
4
Examine the third hadith proof
Read the hadith where the Prophet explicitly declares silk and gold 'haram for the males of my ummah'. This is the most direct proof.
From Abu Dawud.
5
Conclude the ruling
Synthesize the proofs: the prohibition for men is clear and explicit; the permissibility for women is inferred from the Prophet's actions and statements.
This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.

كتاب الحظر والاباحة
[ ٣١٠١ (١) لا يحل للرجال لبس الحوير ويحل للنساء [ ۳۱۰۲ (۲) ولا بأس بتو شده
كتاب الحضر والاباحة )
ضروری نوٹ نظر کے معنی روکنا اور اباحتہ کے معنی مباح ۔ اس کتاب میں بیان کیا جائے گا کہ کون سا کام ممنوع ہے اور کون سا کام مباح ہے۔ [۳۱۰۱] (۱) مرد کے لئے ریشم کا پہننا حرام ہے اور عورت کے لئے حلال ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ عن حذيفة قال نهانا النبي الله الله ان نشرب في آنية الذهب والفضة وان ناكل فيها وعن لبس الحرير والديباج وان نجلس عليه (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب افتراش الحریر، ص ۸۶۸، نمبر ۵۸۳۷ / مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم استعمال اناء الذهب والفضة على الرجال والنساء وخاتم الذهب والحرير على الرجال وا باحته للنساء ، ج ۲، ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۲۴۰۰/۲۰۶۷ / ابو داؤد
شریف ، باب ما جاء في لبس الحریر، ج ۲، ص ۲۰۴ نمبر ۴۰۴۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مردوں کے لئے ریشم کا پہننا حرام ہے۔ عورتوں کے لئے ریشم حلال ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن علی بن ابی طالب قال كساني النبي له حلة سيراء فخرجت فيها فرأيت الغضب في وجهه فشققتها بين نسانی (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الحرير للنساء، ص ۸۶۸، نمبر ۱۵۸۴۰ مسلم شریف، باب تحریم لبس الحرير وغير ذلك للرجال، ج ۲، ص ۱۸۸، نمبر ۲۰۶۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عورتوں کے لئے ریشم حلال ہے (۲) ابوداؤد میں ہے۔ انه سمع علی بن ابی طالب يقول ان نبي الله اخذ حريرا فجعله في يمينه واخذ ذهبا فجعله في شماله ثم قال ان هذين حرام على ذكور امتی (ج) ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب في الحرير للنساء ص ۲۰۶، نمبر ۴۰۵۷) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مرد کے لئے حرام ہے لیکن عورت کے لئے جائز ہے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4, Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah, Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah [3101] (1) It is not permissible for men to wear silk, and it is permissible for women. [3102] (2) There is no harm in using it as a cushion. Kitab al-Hadar wa al-Ibahah: Necessary note: Hazr means prohibition and Ibahah means permissibility. In this book, it will be explained which action is prohibited and which is permissible. [3101] (1) For men, wearing silk is haram, and for women, it is halal. There is a hadith: from Hudhayfah: he said, the Prophet forbade us from drinking in gold and silver vessels, eating in them, and from wearing silk and brocade, and from sitting on them. (a) This hadith indicates that wearing silk is haram for men. For women, silk is halal, and its proof is this hadith: from Ali ibn Abi Talib: he said, the Prophet gave me a silk garment, so I went out wearing it and saw anger on his face, so I tore it and divided it among women. (b) This hadith indicates that silk is halal for women. (2) In Abu Dawud: he heard Ali ibn Abi Talib say that the Prophet took silk in his right hand and gold in his left, then said, 'These two are haram for the males of my ummah.' (c) This hadith also indicates that it is haram for men but permissible for women.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah (Book of Prohibition and Permission) in Al-Sharh al-Thamiri. The author first defines the key terms: hazr means prohibition and ibahah means permissibility. The book will cover which actions are prohibited and which are permissible. Then the first ruling is stated: wearing silk is haram for men and halal for women. The author provides multiple hadith proofs: 1) The well-known hadith of Hudhayfah where the Prophet forbade drinking from gold/silver vessels, eating in them, wearing silk/brocade, and sitting on them. 2) The hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib where the Prophet gave him a silk garment but showed anger when he wore it, so Ali tore it and gave it to women. 3) Another hadith of Ali where the Prophet declared silk and gold haram for the males of his ummah. These hadiths establish the general rule: silk is absolutely forbidden for men in all contexts (except for specific exemptions like war or medical need, to be discussed later), and absolutely permissible for women. The author follows the Hanafi school's position, which holds that the prohibition for men is based on clear hadiths, and the permissibility for women is also based on prophetic practice and explicit statements. The ruling is categorized as haram for men, not merely makruh.

Key Terms
حظر (hazr): Prohibition – an action that is legally forbidden.
اباحة (ibahah): Permissibility – an action that is legally allowed without reward or punishment.
حرام (haram): Strictly forbidden; commission incurs sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib (رضي الله عنه), what did the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) declare about silk and gold?
A) They are halal for both men and women
B) They are haram for men and halal for women
C) They are haram for both men and women
D) They are makruh for men and halal for women

Key Takeaway
Wearing pure silk is haram for men and halal for women, as established by explicit prophetic hadiths.

Leaning on a Silk Cushion: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on leaning on silk cushion with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on leaning on a silk cushion, identify their respective proofs, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A ruling on silk differs by action: wearing is haram for men, but leaning on a silk cushion is makruh according to the Sahibayn, though Abu Hanifa permits it.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a man may lean on a silk cushion. While the prohibition of wearing silk for men is clear, the Sahibayn extend the prohibition to sitting on silk based on a hadith. Abu Hanifa, however, relies on the practice of Ibn Abbas to allow it. Understanding this disagreement reveals how the Hanafi school handles conflicting evidence and the role of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaning on a silk cushion (tawassud). According to Abu Hanifa it is permissible (ja'iz). According to the Sahibayn it is disliked (makruh).
The ruling differs based on the action: wearing silk is haram for men, but leaning is not wearing.
2
Locate the proofs
Abu Hanifa's proof is an athar from Ibn Abbas, who was seen leaning on a silk cushion. The Sahibayn's proof is the hadith of Hudhayfah forbidding sitting on silk.
The athar is a practice of a Companion; the hadith is a direct prohibition from the Prophet.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the Sahibayn, leaning is analogous to sitting, as both involve direct contact with silk for comfort. Abu Hanifa differentiates: wearing is prohibited, but using as a support is not the same.
The Sahibayn apply qiyas; Abu Hanifa restricts the prohibition to its literal scope.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement. The thamarah al-khilaf is the practical ruling: permissible vs. makruh.
Both views are valid within the Hanafi school; later tarjih favors the Sahibayn.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Sahibayn's view is more cautious and widely adopted in later Hanafi fatwa. The mufta bihi is makruh tanzih for men.
Caution (ihtiyat) often prevails in matters of silk due to the strong hadith.

عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله وقالا رحمهما الله يكره تو شده [۳۱۰۳](۳) ولا بأس بلبس الحرير والديباج في الحرب عندهما ويكره عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى. صاحبین فرماتے ہیں ریشم کے تکئے پر ٹیک لگانا مکروہ ہے۔ اوپر بخاری کی حدیث گزری جس میں تھا کہ ریشم پر بیٹھنے سے بھی حضور نے منع فرمایا۔ اس لئے اس کے تکئے پر ٹیک لگانا بھی مکروہ ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن حذيفة قال نهانا النبي الله الله ان نشرب في آنية الذهب والفضة وان ناكل فيها وعن لبس الحرير والديباج وان نجلس عليه (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب افتراش الحریر ص ۸۶۸، نمبر ۵۸۳۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ریشم پر بیٹھنے سے بھی حضور نے منع فرمایا۔ اس لئے ریشم کے تکئے پر ٹیک لگانا بھی مکروہ ہے۔
ت توسد : وسادۃ سے مشتق ہے ٹیک لگانا ، تکیہ بنانا۔
[3102] (2) There is no harm according to Abu Hanifa in leaning on it (a silk cushion), while the Sahibayn say it is disliked (makruh). According to Abu Hanifa, there is no harm in leaning on a silk cushion. In Nasb al-Raya, a narration is transmitted: we were informed by Amr ibn Abi al-Miqdam from Mu'adhdhin of Banu Du'awa: he said I came to Ibn Abbas while he was leaning on a silk cushion, with Sa'id ibn Jubayr at his feet. (d) This athar indicates that there is no harm in leaning on a silk cushion. (Footnotes) (a) Hudhayfah said: the Prophet forbade us from drinking in gold and silver vessels, eating in them, and from wearing silk and brocade, and from sitting on them. (b) Ali said: the Prophet gave me a silk garment, I went out wearing it, saw anger on his face, so I tore it and divided it among women. (c) Ali said: the Prophet took silk in his right hand and gold in his left, then said 'These two are haram for the males of my ummah.' (d) Mu'adhdhin of Banu Du'awa said: I came to Ibn Abbas, he was leaning on a silk cushion, with Sa'id ibn Jubayr at his feet.
(Page 338) Al-Sharh al-Thamiri Part 4, 331, Kitab al-Hazr wa al-Ibahah. According to Abu Hanifa, and according to the Sahibayn, it is disliked to lean on it (a silk cushion). [3103] (3) There is no harm in wearing silk and brocade in war according to them (Sahibayn), and it is disliked according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn say: leaning on a silk cushion is makruh. The hadith mentioned above (Bukhari) prohibits sitting on silk, so leaning on a silk cushion is also makruh. The hadith: from Hudhayfah said: the Prophet forbade us... and from sitting on it. This hadith indicates that sitting on silk is forbidden, so leaning on a silk cushion is also makruh. T-tawassud: derived from wisadah, meaning to lean on, to use as a pillow.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on using a silk cushion (or pillow) for support, specifically leaning on it. The matn states: 'There is no harm in leaning on it according to Abu Hanifa; according to the Sahibayn it is makruh.' The commentary explains the two positions. Abu Hanifa's view is based on an athar from Ibn Abbas, who was seen leaning on a silk cushion. This indicates that leaning on silk is not prohibited. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) consider it makruh because of the general hadith that prohibits sitting on silk. They extend the prohibition of sitting to leaning, since both involve contact with silk for comfort. The commentary on page 338 reiterates the Sahibayn's argument: the hadith of Hudhayfah explicitly forbids sitting on silk, so leaning on a silk cushion falls under the same ruling. The note on 'توسد' clarifies that it means to lean on or use as a pillow. The dispute is intra-Hanafi: Abu Hanifa prioritizes the specific practice of a Companion (Ibn Abbas) over a general analogy, while the Sahibayn prioritize the apparent meaning of the hadith. The mufta bihi position in later Hanafi works tends to follow the Sahibayn, makruh tanzihan for men (since wearing silk for men is haram, but using it as a pillow is only makruh because it is not wearing). For women, it is permissible according to all.

Key Terms
توسد (tawassud): To lean on or use as a pillow (from wisadah, cushion).
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; an action that is not haram but should be avoided. In Hanafi terminology, makruh tahrimi is close to haram, while makruh tanzih is less severe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the Sahibayn's ruling that leaning on a silk cushion is makruh?
A) The hadith forbidding drinking from gold vessels
B) The hadith forbidding sitting on silk
C) The athar from Ibn Abbas
D) Qiyas with wearing silk

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school differs on whether men may lean on silk cushions: Abu Hanifa permits it based on an athar, while the Sahibayn consider it makruh based on the hadith forbidding sitting on silk. The mufta bihi is makruh tanzih.

Ruling on Wearing Silk in War
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proof texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing silk in war, explain the proofs of the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In war, silk is permissible for men due to necessity, though Abu Hanifa disliked it.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi difference on a practical battlefield issue: may a man wear silk garments in war? The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) permit it, while Imam Abu Hanifa considers it makruh. The commentary marshals proof texts and rational arguments to support the prevailing view of the Sahibayn, which is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the ruling of the Sahibayn (no harm/permissible) and of Abu Hanifa (makruh). Note the difference in authority: the Sahibayn represent the majority Hanafi position, while Abu Hanifa's view is a minority within the school.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab dispute.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proofs
The passage cites three proofs: (1) an athar from Ata ibn Abi Rabah permitting silk in war, (2) practical benefits (sword slides off silk, sheen intimidates enemy), (3) a hadith where the Prophet allowed silk for scabies, analogized to the greater need in war.
The qiyas from the scabies hadith is a key argument: if a minor excuse permits silk, a major necessity (self-preservation) permits it a fortiori.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa adheres to the general prohibition of silk for men and considers the war context insufficient to override it entirely. He cites an athar from Ikrimah who disliked silk in war, saying it detracts from the spirit of martyrdom.
Abu Hanifa does not declare it haram; he categorizes it as makruh, indicating a degree of flexibility.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to the Sahibayn, a man may wear silk in battle without sin; according to Abu Hanifa, it is better to avoid it, but doing so is not sinful.
The thamarah is a difference in ethical recommendation, not in legal validity.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of the Sahibayn: permissible. This is due to the strength of their evidence (hadith and practical reasoning) and the general need for protection in war.
The author of this sharh supports the Sahibayn, and this is the standard Hanafi teaching.

(3) In a hadith, permission for silk was given due to scabies, and in war there is greater need, so permission for wearing silk is given. The hadith: from Anas that Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and Zubayr complained to the Prophet about lice, so he permitted them to wear silk, and I saw them wearing it in a battle. (c) (Bukhari, chapter on silk in war, p. 409, no. 2920; Abu Dawud, chapter on wearing silk due to excuse, p. 206, no. 4056; Tirmidhi, chapter on concession for wearing silk in war, p. 1302, no. 1722) This hadith shows that one may wear silk due to an excuse like scabies. And in the hadith of Tirmidhi and Bukhari, there is explicit mention that the Companions used to wear it in war. Imam Abu Hanifa, based on the hadith of prohibition, considers wearing silk in war as makruh. Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on men wearing silk in battle. The matn states: 'No harm in wearing silk and brocade in war according to the Sahibayn; according to Abu Hanifa it is makruh.' The commentary provides the proofs for the Sahibayn's position. First, an athar from Ata ibn Abi Rabah that there is no harm in wearing silk in war. Second, practical benefits: silk is slippery, causing swords to slide off, and its sheen intimidates the enemy. Third, a hadith from Anas: the Prophet allowed Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and Zubayr to wear silk due to scabies, and they wore it in battle. The commentary argues that if a minor excuse like scabies permits silk, then the greater need for protection in war also permits it. The Sahibayn rely on these concessions and the general principle of necessity (darurah). Abu Hanifa, however, adheres to the general hadith prohibiting silk for men, considering the war situation as a possible excuse but not sufficient to make it permissible; he classifies it as makruh (disliked) rather than haram, but closer to prohibition. The athar from Ikrimah supports Abu Hanifa: he disliked it, saying wearing silk in war delays martyrdom (since silk is comfortable and shows status). The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is the Sahibayn's view: it is permissible to wear silk in war due to need. For women, it is absolutely permissible in all cases.

Key Terms
ديباج (dibaj): Brocade, a type of silk fabric.
عذر (udhr): Excuse; valid reason allowing relaxation of a ruling, such as illness or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence used by the Sahibayn to permit wearing silk in war?
A) The hadith of Hudhayfah forbidding silk
B) The athar from Ikrimah disliking it
C) The hadith of Anas about permission for scabies
D) Qiyas with wearing gold

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is that men may wear silk in war due to necessity, based on the Sahibayn's proofs.

Ruling on Reclining on Silk Cushions and Wearing Silk in War
Intra-Hanafi dispute on silk in war with agreed ruling on silk cushions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reclining on silk cushions and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on wearing silk in war, identifying the proof for each position.

Core Idea
Reclining on silk cushions is disliked; silk in war splits the school: Sahibayn permit, Abu Hanifa dislikes.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri addresses two issues related to silk garments for men. The first, reclining on a silk cushion, is unanimously considered disliked. The second, wearing silk in war, reveals a disagreement within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this difference requires careful consideration of the proofs each side relies on.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling
Determine the ruling on reclining on a silk cushion according to both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Note the hadith evidence cited.
The hadith forbids sitting on silk; reclining is analogous.
2
Locate the disputed issue
Recognize that the dispute concerns wearing silk in war. Abu Hanifa says it is disliked; the Sahibayn say there is no harm.
3
State Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the general prohibition of silk for men and the athar of Ikrimah who disliked silk in war.
He considers the general prohibition overriding the war exception.
4
State the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cite the hadith of permission for scabies, the practice of Companions wearing silk in battle, and the athar of Ata' allowing it.
They see war as a necessity that permits silk.
5
Analyze the disagreement
Contrast the two approaches: one prioritizes the general prohibition, the other prioritizes specific exceptions and necessities.
The thamarah al-khilaf is a practical difference in fatwa.

رخص في لبس الحرير في الحرب اذا كان له عذر ، ج خامس ص ۱۵۴، نمبر ۲۴۶۶۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جنگ میں ریشم پہننا مکروہ ہے۔
Book of Prohibitions and Permissibility. According to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) and they both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said (may Allah have mercy on them both): He dislikes reclining on a cushion [3103](3). And there is no harm in wearing silk and dibaj in war according to them, and it is disliked according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah Almighty have mercy on him). The two companions say: Reclining on a silk cushion is disliked. Above, the hadith of Bukhari passed which stated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade sitting on silk. Therefore, reclining on its cushion is also disliked. The hadith is: From Hudhayfah, he said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade us from drinking in vessels of gold and silver, and eating in them, and from wearing silk and dibaj, and from sitting on it. (Bukhari, Chapter on Spreading Silk, p. 868, no. 5837). This hadith shows that the Prophet forbade sitting on silk. Therefore, reclining on a silk cushion is also disliked. Tawassud: Derived from wisadah, meaning to recline, to make a pillow. (13103)(3) There is no harm in wearing silk and dibaj in war according to the two, and it is disliked according to Imam Abu Hanifa. In the battlefield, silk and dibaj are silken garments; wearing them according to the two companions is not objectionable. From Ata', he said: There is no harm in wearing silk in war. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, from those who permitted wearing silk in war if there is an excuse, vol. 5, p. 153, no. 24663 / Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on Silk and Dibaj and Gold and Silver Vessels, vol. 11, no. 19943) This athar shows that wearing silk in war is permissible. (2) The silk garment, if not woven tightly, causes the sword to slip, so wearing it saves life. Second, its shine intimidates the enemy, so there is allowance for wearing it. (3) There is a hadith that due to scabies, silk was permitted, and in war there is greater need, so permission to wear silk will be given. The hadith is: From Anas, that Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and al-Zubayr complained to the Prophet (peace be upon him) about lice, so he permitted them to wear silk, and I saw them wearing it in a battle. (Bukhari, Chapter on Silk in War, p. 409, no. 2920; Abu Dawud, Chapter on Wearing Silk for an Excuse, p. 206, no. 4056; Tirmidhi, Chapter on the Concession for Wearing Silk in War, p. 1302, no. 1722) This hadith shows that due to the excuse of scabies, one can wear silk. And in the hadith of Tirmidhi and Bukhari, there is explicit mention that the Companions used to wear it in battle. Imam Abu Hanifa, based on the hadith of prohibition, considers wearing silk in war as disliked. There is also another athar: From Ikrimah, that he disliked it in war and said: He is most hopeful of martyrdom. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah from footnote: (a) Hudhayfah said: The Prophet forbade me from drinking from vessels of gold and silver, and eating in them, and from wearing silk and dibaj, and from sitting on them. (b) Ata' said: There is no harm in wearing silk in war. (c) Abd al-Rahman and Zubayr complained about lice, so he permitted them both to wear silk. Then I saw them wearing silk in Ghumra? (d) Ikrimah disliked silk in war and said he hopes for martyrdom. (Continued on next page)
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 4, p. 332, Book of Prohibitions and Permissibility. He permitted wearing silk in war if there is an excuse, vol. 5, p. 154, no. 24666) From this athar it is understood that wearing silk in war is disliked.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri treats two rulings related to silk for men. First, the ruling on reclining on a silk cushion: the text states that according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is disliked (makruh). The proof is the hadith of Hudhayfah where the Prophet forbade sitting on silk. Since reclining is a form of sitting, the same prohibition applies. Second, the ruling on wearing silk in war: here there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The Sahibayn consider it permissible (la ba'sa) because the hadith allowing silk for scabies indicates that necessity permits it, and war is a greater necessity. They also cite the practice of Companions wearing silk in battle. Abu Hanifa, however, maintains that it remains disliked (makruh) based on the general prohibition of silk for men. He supports his view with the athar from Ikrimah who disliked silk in war. The passage does not indicate which position is mufta bihi (preferred for fatwa). It is important to note that both schools agree on the principle that silk is generally prohibited for men, but they differ on the exception for war.

Key Terms
توسد (tawassud): Reclining on a cushion or pillow, making something a pillow.
حرير (harir): Silk, a fabric produced from silkworms, prohibited for men in general.
ديباج (dibaj): A type of silk brocade, often with patterns.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on reclining on a silk cushion according to both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Disliked (makruh)
C) Prohibited (haram)
D) Recommended (mandub)

Key Takeaway
Reclining on silk cushions is makruh by agreement; wearing silk in war is subject to ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa (makruh) and the Sahibayn (permissible).

Wearing Mulham: Hanafi Ruling on Silk-Mixed Fabrics
Ruling on permissibility of wearing fabric with silk warp and cotton/wool weft

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing mulham fabric and explain the legal reasoning based on weft dominance, and apply it to similar mixed-fabric cases.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a fabric's ruling on silk prohibition depends on the weft, not the warp — mulham is permissible because its weft is cotton or wool.

This passage addresses a common question: Is it permissible for men to wear fabric that contains silk threads? In Hanafi fiqh, the answer depends on which threads dominate the fabric's structure. The author explains that the weft (lakhma) is the decisive component, not the warp (sada). Therefore, mulham – fabric with a silk warp and non-silk weft – is permissible. The ruling is supported by a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ and the practice of Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being judged? The act of wearing mulham. The ruling: no harm (la ba's), i.e., permissible (mubah).
Mulham is defined as fabric with a silk warp and a weft of cotton or wool.
2
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
Why is it permissible? The fabric is identified by its weft, not its warp. Since the weft is non-silk, the fabric is legally considered cotton or wool.
The principle: 'al-ibratu fi al-sawbi bi al-lakhma' (consideration is given to the weft).
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The author cites a hadith: the Prophet ﷺ clothed a man with a turban of khazz (a silk-wool mix). This indicates permissibility of mixed fabrics.
Khazz originally meant silk-wool blend; here it extends to silk-cotton blends.
4
Note the broader evidence
The Companions, including Anas and al-Bara' ibn 'Azib, wore khazz. Abu Bakrah had a garment of khazz with silk warp.
This shows practical acceptance of such fabrics.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may consider any silk presence sufficient for prohibition. The Hanafi school gives weight to the weft.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۱۰۴(۴) ولا بأس بلبس الملحم اذا كان سداه ابريسمًا ولحمته قطنا او خرا (۱۳۱۰۴ (۴) اور کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے ہم کے پہنے میں جبکہ اس کا تا ناریشم ہواور باناسوت یا اون ہو۔ کپڑے تانے سے نہیں بنتا بلکہ بانے سے بنتا ہے اس لئے اصل اعتبار بانے کا ہے۔ پس اگر با ناسوت یا اون کا ہو تو وہ سوت یا اون ہی شمار ہوگا ریشم شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لئے تا نا چا ہے ریشم ہو لیکن باتا اگر اون یا سوت ہے تو اس کے پہننے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ اخبرنی عبد الله بن سعيد عن ابيه سعد قال رأيت رجلا ببخارى على بغلة بيضاء عليه عمامة خز سوداء فقال كسانیها رسول الله الا الله) الف) دوسری روایت کے اخیر میں ہے۔ قال ابو داؤد وعشرون نفسا من اصحاب رسول الله له او اكثر لبسوا الخز منهم انش، والبراء بن عازب (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الخز، ج ۲، ص ۲۰۴ نمبر ۴۰۳۸) (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ كان لابي بكرة مطرف خز سداه حرير وكان يلبسه (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی هیة ، امن رخص في لبس الحرير : امس، ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۲۴۶۱۶) اس حدیث اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ خز یعنی ایسا کپڑا جس میں ریشم اور اور ان دونوں ہوں یا ریشم اور ست دونوں ہوں ان کا پہننا جائز ہے۔ اون اور ریشم دونوں کے مجموعی کپڑے کو خز کہتے ہیں۔
انه سرا : تانا، لحمه : بانا، ابریسم : ریشم قطن : روئی۔
[13104](4) And there is no harm in wearing mulham when its warp is silk and its weft is cotton or wool. (13104)(4) And there is no harm in wearing mulham when its warp is silk and its weft is cotton or wool. The two companions say: There is no harm in wearing mulham when its warp is silk and its weft is cotton or wool. Clothing is not made from the warp but from the weft, so consideration is given to the weft. So if the weft is cotton or wool, it is considered cotton or wool, not silk. Therefore, even if the warp is silk, if the weft is wool or cotton, there is no harm in wearing it. There is a hadith: Abdallah ibn Sa'id narrated from his father Sa'd: I saw a man in Bukhara on a white mule with a black turban of khazz, and he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) clothed me with it. (a) In another narration: Abu Dawud said: Twenty or more Companions of the Messenger of Allah wore khazz, among them Anas and al-Bara' ibn 'Azib. (b) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Khazz, vol. 2, p. 204, no. 4038) (2) There is an athar: Abu Bakrah had a garment of khazz whose warp was silk, and he wore it. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, from those who permitted wearing silk, p. 149, no. 24616) From this hadith and athar it is understood that khazz, i.e., a garment containing both silk and wool or silk and cotton, is permissible to wear. A garment made of both wool and silk is called khazz. Its warp: the warp; its weft: the weft; abrisam: silk; qutn: cotton.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on mulham, a fabric with a silk warp and a non-silk weft (cotton or wool). The ruling is that it is permissible for men to wear. The reasoning is that clothing is primarily defined by the weft, not the warp. Since the weft is cotton or wool, the fabric is considered cotton or wool, not silk, and thus not subject to the prohibition of silk for men. The author supports this with a hadith about the Prophet clothing a man with a turban of khazz (a mixed fabric), and reports that many Companions wore khazz. The term 'khazz' originally refers to a mixture of silk and wool, but here it includes silk-cotton blends as well. The key principle is that legal consideration is given to the dominant or functionally significant component. This ruling is a clear statement without dispute within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ملحم (mulham): A fabric with a silk warp and a cotton or wool weft.
سدى (sada): The warp threads in weaving.
لحمة (lihma): The weft threads in weaving.
خز (khazz): A garment woven from a mixture of silk and wool (or cotton).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what determines whether a mixed-fabric garment is permissible for men?
A) The presence of any silk
B) The type of weft (cotton or wool)
C) The color of the fabric
D) Whether it is imported

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of mulham rests on the weft being non-silk, demonstrating the Hanafi principle of giving legal weight to the dominant component.

Prohibition of Gold and Silver Jewelry for Men
Ruling with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that gold and silver jewelry is haram for men, identify the exception for a silver ring of one mithqal, and cite the supporting hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Gold and silver jewelry is haram for men; only a silver ring of one mithqal is halal.

This lesson examines the clear prohibition of men adorning themselves with gold and silver, a ruling that parallels the prohibition of silk for men. The Hanafi school provides a narrow exception for a silver ring of one mithqal. We will explore the textual proofs from authentic hadith that establish this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the act of tahalli (adorning oneself) with gold and silver for men. The hukm is haram, with an exception for a silver ring of one mithqal.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: one from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari in Tirmidhi explicitly forbidding silk and gold for males, and another from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib in Bukhari listing the gold ring among forbidden items.
Both hadith are ahad (single-chain), giving them zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'harrama' (he forbade) indicates clear prohibition. The gender specification ('dhukur ummati' vs. 'inathim') shows the ruling is specific to men.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۱۰۵) (۵) ولا يجوز للرجال التحلّى بالذهب والفضة. جس طرح عورتوں کے لئے ریشم پہننا جائز ہے اسی طرح ان کے لئے سونے اور چاندی کا زیور پہننا جائز ہے۔ اور جس طرح مرد کے لئے ریشم پہننا حرام ہے اسی طرح ان کے لئے سونے اور چاندی کے زیور پہننا حرام ہے۔ البتہ صرف چاندی کی ایک تولہ انگوٹھی پہننا حلال ہے

[13105](5) And it is not permissible for men to adorn themselves with gold and silver. Just as wearing silk is permissible for women, similarly wearing gold and silver jewelry is permissible for them. And just as wearing silk is forbidden for men, similarly wearing gold and silver jewelry is forbidden for them. However, wearing a silver ring of one mithqal is permissible. In a hadith: From Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: He forbade the wearing of silk and gold for the males of my ummah and permitted it for their females. (Tirmidhi, Chapter on Silk and Gold for Men, p. 302, no. 1720) (2) Another hadith: I heard al-Bara' ibn 'Azib say: The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade us from seven things: he forbade the gold ring, or the gold signet ring, and silk, and istabraq, and dibaj, and the red saddle cloth, and qassiy, and silver vessels. (Bukhari, Chapter on Gold Signet Rings, p. 1871, no. 5863)
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage states the clear Hanafi ruling that men are prohibited from wearing gold and silver jewelry. The reasoning parallels the prohibition of silk for men: just as silk is forbidden for men but permitted for women, so too gold and silver adornment. An exception is made for a silver ring weighing one mithqal (approximately 4.8 grams), which is permissible. The proof is provided by two hadith: one from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari explicitly stating that silk and gold are forbidden for males and allowed for females, and another from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib listing the gold ring among forbidden items. These hadith are from sound collections (Tirmidhi and Bukhari). The commentary emphasizes that the prohibition is general, with only a narrow exception for a simple silver ring.

Key Terms
تحلى (tahalli): Adorning oneself with jewelry or ornaments.
ذهب (dhahab): Gold, a precious metal; its use as jewelry is prohibited for men.
فضة (fidda): Silver; its use as jewelry is prohibited for men except for a ring of one mithqal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Wearing Mulham (Silk Warp, Cotton Weft) is Permissible
Ruling with proof on mulham permissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mulham fabric and explain the legal basis focusing on the weft (luhmah).

Core Idea
A garment is judged by its weft, not its warp – silk in the warp does not affect permissibility.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling on mixed silk fabrics. The Hanafi school permits men to wear mulham—a fabric with a silk warp and cotton or wool weft. The key legal principle is that the garment is classified by its weft material. We will look at the proof from hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Mulham is a fabric with a silk warp (sada) and a weft (luhmah) of cotton or wool. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) for men to wear.
The ruling is explicitly stated in the opening line: 'لا بأس بلبس الملحم' – there is no harm.
2
Locate the dalil
Two proofs are cited: a hadith from Sa'd about a khazz turban given by the Prophet (ﷺ), and an athar that Abu Bakrah wore a khazz cloak with silk warp.
Reference: Sunan Abi Dawud, Bab ma ja'a fi al-khazz, no. 4038; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 24616.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith shows the Prophet (ﷺ) himself gave and wore khazz, a mixed fabric of silk and wool/cotton. The athar confirms Companions wore it. This indicates permissibility despite silk being present in the warp.
The commentary explains that the legal consideration ('i'tibar) is given to the weft because the fabric is woven from the weft.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may consider any presence of silk problematic, but the Hanafi school distinguishes based on which component is used in the weft.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the broader scope of silk rulings.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that mulham is permissible for men if the weft is not silk, regardless of the warp material.
This is the position presented in the text and supported by the proofs.

Source Text

رخص في لبس الحرير في الحرب اذا كان له عذر ، ج خامس ص ۱۵۴، نمبر ۲۴۶۶۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جنگ میں ریشم پہننا مکروہ ہے۔ (۱۳۱۰۴ (۴) اور کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے ہم کے پہنے میں جبکہ اس کا تا ناریشم ہواور باناسوت یا اون ہو۔ کپڑے تانے سے نہیں بنتا بلکہ بانے سے بنتا ہے اس لئے اصل اعتبار بانے کا ہے۔ پس اگر با ناسوت یا اون کا ہو تو وہ سوت یا اون ہی شمار ہوگا ریشم شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ اس لئے تا نا چا ہے ریشم ہو لیکن باتا اگر اون یا سوت ہے تو اس کے پہننے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ اخبرني عبد الله بن سعيد عن ابيه سعد قال رأيت رجلا ببخارى على بغلة بيضاء عليه عمامة خز سوداء فقال كسانيها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم) الف) دوسری روایت کے اخیر میں ہے۔ قال ابو داؤد وعشرون نفسا من اصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اكثر لبسوا الخز منهم انس، والبراء بن عازب (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الخز، ج ۲، ص ۲۰۴ نمبر ۴۰۳۸) (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ كان لابي بكرة مطرف خز سداه حرير وكان يلبسه (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شيبة، امن رخص في لبس الحرير : امس، ص ۱۴۹ نمبر ۲۴۶۱۶) اس حدیث اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ خز یعنی ایسا کپڑا جس میں ریشم اور اور ان دونوں ہوں یا ریشم اور ست دونوں ہوں ان کا پہننا جائز ہے۔ اون اور ریشم دونوں کے مجموعی کپڑے کو خز کہتے ہیں۔

And the athar: 'Abu Bakrah had a cloak of khazz whose warp was silk, and he used to wear it.'
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This is a ruling on the permissibility of wearing mulham, a fabric with a silk warp and a weft of cotton or wool. The commentary explains that the legal consideration is given to the weft, not the warp, because fabric is woven from the weft. Thus, if the weft is cotton or wool, the garment is considered cotton or wool, and wearing it is permissible even if the warp is silk. The ruling is supported by the hadith of Sa'd about a khazz turban and the athar of Abu Bakrah, indicating that khazz (a mixed fabric of silk and wool/cotton) is permissible. The text also notes that there is a dispensation for wearing silk in battle if one has an excuse, but that is not the main point here.

Key Terms
الملحم (al-mulham): A fabric with silk warp and cotton or wool weft.
السدى (al-sada): The warp threads in weaving.
اللحمة (al-luhmah): The weft threads in weaving.
الخز (al-khazz): A garment woven with silk and wool or cotton; a type of mixed fabric.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on mulham is based on the weft material: if the weft is not silk, the garment is permissible regardless of the warp.

Gold and Silver Adornment Prohibited for Men
Ruling with hadith evidence prohibiting men from gold/silver ornaments, with exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on gold and silver ornaments for men, cite the hadith evidence, and identify the exception for a silver ring.

Core Idea
Gold and silver ornaments are haram for men except a silver ring; the prohibition is proven by explicit hadith.

This passage addresses a clear-cut prohibition in Hanafi fiqh: men may not wear gold or silver ornaments. The ruling is supported by two authentic hadith that categorically forbid gold (including rings) and silk for males, while permitting them for females. An exception is made for a silver ring of one tola or less, which is halal for men.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being prohibited? For whom? The text states 'it is not permissible for men to adorn themselves with gold and silver.'
Note the gender-specific prohibition.
2
Note the gender distinction
The commentary draws an analogy with silk: just as silk is halal for women and haram for men, gold and silver ornaments are halal for women and haram for men.
This analogy reinforces the rule.
3
Examine the exception
The only exception is a silver ring of one tola (approx. 11.66g) or less. This is explicitly stated as halal for men.
No other silver ornaments are exempted.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: (1) Abu Musa al-Ash'ari reports the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade silk and gold for males. (2) Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib reports the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited seven things including the gold ring, silk, and silver vessels. These clearly indicate prohibition.
The first hadith uses the word 'harrama' (forbade), which carries a strong legal weight.
5
Consider consensus
There is no internal Hanafi dispute; all Hanafi authorities agree on this prohibition. The exception for the silver ring is also well-established.
Thus, the ruling is reliable and operative.

مسلم شریف، باب تحریم استعمال اناء الذهب والفضة على الرجال والنساء الخ، ج ۲ ص ۱۸۸ نمبر ۶۶ ۲۰) ان دونوں حدیثوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرد کے لئے سونے اور چاندی کا زیور پہنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
تحملی : علی سے مشتق ہے زیور پہننا، الذهب : سونا، الفضة : چاندی۔
And it is not permissible for men to adorn themselves with gold and silver. ... The hadith from Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'The wearing of silk and gold is forbidden for the males of my Ummah and permitted for its females.' ... Another hadith: I heard al-Bara' ibn 'Azib say: The Prophet (ﷺ) forbade us seven things: he forbade the gold ring, or he said the gold ring, and silk, and istabraq, and dibaj, and red mitharah, and qasi, and silver vessels. These two hadiths show that it is not permissible for men to wear gold and silver ornaments.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This is a ruling prohibiting men from wearing ornaments made of gold or silver. The commentary first notes that just as silk is permissible for women and impermissible for men, similarly gold and silver ornaments are permissible for women but impermissible for men. However, an exception is made for a silver ring of one tola weight, which is halal for men. The ruling is supported by two hadiths: (1) Abu Musa al-Ash'ari reports that the Prophet (ﷺ) declared silk and gold forbidden for males and allowed for females. (2) Al-Bara' ibn 'Azib reports that the Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited seven things including the gold ring, silk, istabraq (thick silk), dibaj (brocade), red mitharah (saddle cloth), qasi (a type of garment), and silver vessels. These indicate the prohibition of gold and silver ornaments for men. The text also explains the derivation of the word 'tahalli' (ادornment) from 'aliyya'.

Key Terms
التحلي (al-tahalli): Adorning oneself with ornaments.
الذهب (al-dhahab): Gold.
الفضة (al-fiddah): Silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a man wearing a gold necklace?
A) Permissible, because gold is not specifically mentioned for men.
B) Haram, based on the hadith of Abu Musa.
C) Makruh tanzihi, because it resembles women.
D) Permissible only if the gold is less than one tola.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits gold and silver ornaments for men, except a silver ring of one tola or less, based on explicit hadith.

Silver Ring, Belt, and Sword Ornamentation Permissible
Ruling with proof on permissibility of silver items for men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on silver rings, belts, and sword fittings for men and identify the prophetic proofs (dalil) and analogy (qiyas) used to derive it.

Core Idea
Silver rings, belts, and sword fittings are permissible for men by prophetic example and analogy.

This passage addresses a common question: what forms of silver may a man use? The Hanafi school permits the use of silver in functional or decorative items like rings, belts, and sword ornamentation. The ruling is based on specific hadith and analogy. Understanding the proofs and the scope of permissibility helps avoid confusion with the prohibition of gold.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items and the ruling
The text explicitly mentions three items: ring (khatam), belt (mintaqah), and sword ornamentation (hilyat al-sayf). The ruling is that there is no harm (la ba's) – i.e., permissible (mubah).
The ruling covers only these specific forms of silver usage.
2
Locate the dalil for the ring
The author cites a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet initially wore a gold ring, then discarded it and adopted a silver ring. This establishes the permissibility of a silver ring.
The hadith is found in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
3
Examine the dalil for the sword
A hadith from Anas reports that the pommel of the Prophet's sword was silver. This directly shows that silver may be used on swords.
This hadith is from Abu Dawud and Nasa'i.
4
Understand the qiyas for the belt
No direct hadith mentions a silver belt. Instead, the author uses qiyas from the sword (asl) to the belt (far') because both are functional items that require silver for practical or decorative purposes. Additionally, the hadith of the Prophet's cup repaired with silver supports the permissibility of silver on everyday tools.
The illa (effective cause) is functionality – the item serves a purpose beyond adornment.
5
Note the scope and limitations
The permissibility is limited to these functional items. Pure adornment (e.g., silver necklace for men) is not covered by these proofs and requires separate evaluation.
The text emphasises that the silver used is minimal ('as a sample').

Source Text

[۳۱۰۶] (۶) ولابأس بالخاتم والمنطقة وحلية السيف من الفضة.
ت انگوٹھی چاندی کی ہو یا پڑکا چاندی کا ہو یا تلوار میں چاندی کا زیور لگا ہو تو اس کے استعمال کرنے میں کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے سونے کی انگوٹھی بنوائی پھر اس کو پھینک دیا اور چاندی کی انگوٹھی بنوائی ۔ عن عبد الله ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اتخذ خاتما من ذهب وجعل فصه مما يلى كفه فاتخذه الناس فرمي به واتخذ خاتما من ورق أو فضة (الف) (بخاری شریف، باب خواتیم الذهب، ص ۸۷۱، نمبر ۵۸۶۵ر مسلم شریف ، باب خاتم الورق قصہ بشی ، ص ۱۹۶، نمبر ۲۰۹۴ را بو داؤد شریف باب ما جاء فى اتخاذ الخاتم ص ۲۲۷ نمبر ۴۲۱۴ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرد چاندی کی انگوٹھی بنوا سکتا ہے۔ تلوار میں چاندی کے زیور کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن انس قال كانت قبيعة سيف رسول الله فضة (ب) (ابود او دشریف، باب فی السیف محلی می ۱۳۵۵، نمبر ۲۵۸۳ نسائی شریف، باب حلیۃ السیف ص ۷۲۸ نمبر ۵۳۷۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تلوار میں چاندی ہو اس کے دستے میں چاندی ہو تو جائز ہے۔ اور پلکے کو اس پر قیاس کر سکتے ہیں۔ عن عاصم الاحول قال رأيت قدح النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عند انس بن مالك وكان قد انصدع فسلسله بفضة قال هو قدح جيد عريض من نضار قال قال انس لقد سقيت رسول الله في هذا القدح اكثر من كذا و كذا (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الشرب من قدح النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم، ص۸۴۲، نمبر ۵۶۳۸) اس حدیث میں ٹوٹے ہوئے پیالے پر چاندی چڑایا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ پٹکے پر چاندی لگانا جائز ہے (۳) اصل میں نمونے کے طور پر چاندی استعمال کرنا جائز ہے۔ اور اتنی ہی چاندی نمونے کے طور پر ہی ہوتی ہے اس لئے اتنی چاندی کا استعمال جائز ہے۔
ت منطقه : پٹکا، حلیۃ السیف : تلوار کا زیور
And there is no harm in the ring, the belt, and the ornamentation of the sword made of silver. ... The hadith from 'Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) took a ring of gold, then he threw it away and took a ring of silver. ... The hadith from Anas: The pommel of the Prophet's sword was silver. ... The hadith from 'Asim al-Ahwal: I saw the cup of the Prophet (ﷺ) with Anas ibn Malik, and it had cracked, so he repaired it with silver. From this, it is known that applying silver to the belt is permissible.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This ruling states that there is no harm in men using a ring, a belt, or sword ornamentation made of silver. The commentary explains that a silver ring is permissible based on the hadith that the Prophet (ﷺ) set aside a gold ring and adopted a silver one. For the sword, the hadith of Anas that the pommel of the Prophet's sword was silver is cited. By analogy (qiyas), the same applies to a belt, as evidenced by the hadith of the Prophet's cup which had a crack repaired with silver. The principle is that using silver for functional or ornamental purposes (as a repair or in small quantities for use) is permissible. The text also notes that silver used in these items is typically minimal and for necessity, not for extravagant adornment.

Key Terms
الخاتم (al-khatam): Ring.
المنطقة (al-mintaqah): Belt or waistband.
حلية السيف (hilyat al-sayf): Ornamentation of the sword, such as pommel, hilt, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A silver belt

D) A silver sword hilt

Key Takeaway
Silver rings, belts, and sword fittings are permissible for men based on prophetic example and analogy, while gold items are prohibited.

Gold and Silver Adornment Permissible for Women
Ruling with proof: permissibility for women derived from explicit hadith exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women wearing gold and silver and identify the explicit hadith that establishes this permissibility.

Core Idea
Gold and silver adornment is specifically permitted for women by explicit hadith exception, while haram for men.

This passage presents a clear ruling that women may adorn themselves with gold and silver. It is based on the well-known hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, which explicitly permits these metals for the females of the Ummah while forbidding them for males. The ruling is straightforward and agreed upon by all major schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is al-tahalli (adorning oneself) with gold and silver. For women, this ruling is permissible (mubah) based on the text.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, which is a hadith ahad but clear in its meaning.
The hadith is recorded in Sunan al-Tirmidhi, among others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'wa ahalla li-inathihim' (and permitted for its females), which directly establishes permissibility for women.
The wording is explicit (nass) and leaves no room for interpretation.
4
Note the contrast for men
The same hadith also states 'harrama libasa al-hariri wa al-dhahabi 'ala dhukuri ummati' (forbade the wearing of silk and gold for the males of my Ummah), confirming the gender distinction.
5
Confirm the consensus
There is no ikhtilaf among the four schools on this ruling; it is agreed upon (muttafaq alayh).
Some minor differences exist on the exact definition of gold/silver alloys, but the permissibility for women is universal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۰۷(۷) ويجوز للنساء التحلّى بالذهب والفضة .
حدیث میں پہلے گزر چکا کہ عورتوں کے لئے سونا اور چاندی کا زیور پہنا جائز ہے۔ عن ابی موسی اشعری ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال حرم لباس الحرير والذهب على ذكور امتى واحل لاناثهم ( د )
حاشیہ : (پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے) سونے کے حلقے سے، ریشم سے، استبرق سے، دیباج سے سرخ میٹرہ سے کسی سے، چاندی کے برتن سے (الف) آپ نے سونے کی انگوٹی بنائی اور اس کا مینہ تھیلی کی طرف کیا تو لوگوں نے بھی انگوٹھی بنائی۔ پھر آپ نے اس کو پھینک دیا اور چاندی کی انگوٹھی بنائی (ب) حضرت انس فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور کی تلوار کا دستہ چاندی کا تھا (ج) حضرت عاصم فرماتے ہیں کہ میں حضرت انس کے پاس حضور کا پیالہ دیکھا اس کا ایک کنارہ ٹوٹ گیا تھا جس کو چاندی سے باندھا تھا۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ ایک چھوٹا سا پیالہ تھ چوڑا تھا اور جھاؤ کی لکڑی کا تھا۔ حضرت انس فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور گو اس پیالے سے اتنے اتنے مرتبہ پلایا ہے۔
And it is permissible for women to adorn themselves with gold and silver. The hadith has already passed that it is permissible for women to wear gold and silver ornaments. From Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'The wearing of silk and gold is forbidden for the males of my Ummah and permitted for its females.'
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This ruling explicitly permits women to adorn themselves with gold and silver ornaments. The commentary refers back to the same hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari that was cited in the previous ruling for men, which states that silk and gold are forbidden for men but allowed for women. Thus, the permissibility for women is derived from the explicit exception in the hadith. The footnote repeats the hadith and also includes other narrations that were mentioned earlier, emphasizing that the prohibition of gold and silver is specific to men, and women are exempted.

Key Terms
التحلى (al-tahalli): Adorning oneself with ornaments.
الذهب (al-dhahab): Gold, a precious metal.
الفضة (al-fidda): Silver, a precious metal.

Key Takeaway
Women are explicitly permitted to wear gold and silver based on the hadith of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.

Ruling on Employing Eunuchs
Ruling on eunuch employment with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that employing eunuchs is makruh in the Hanafi school and explain the reason based on the hadith prohibiting castration.

Core Idea
Using eunuchs as servants is disliked because it encourages the prohibited act of castration.

This passage addresses the ruling on taking service from eunuchs (castrated men). The author explains that doing so is disliked because it indirectly promotes the act of castration, which is prohibited in hadith. Understanding this ruling helps students see how secondary acts are evaluated based on their connection to prohibited actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act under discussion is employing a eunuch (khasi) as a servant.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is makruh (disliked). Specifically, it is considered makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school.
The text uses the term 'makruh', but the context implies a strong dislike due to connection with a prohibited act.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet prohibited castration of horses and animals.
The hadith is transmitted in Musnad Ahmad and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of castration indicates that any act encouraging it, such as employing eunuchs, is disliked. The reasoning is that employing them implicitly supports the practice of castration.
This is an example of sadd al-dhara'i (blocking the means to evil).
5
Note cross-madhhab status
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed) among schools; some may consider it merely makruh tanzihi or even permissible.

ت زخرفتہ : خوبصورت بنانا، مزین کرنا۔
(۱۳۱۱۴ (۱۴) مکروہ ہے خصی سے خدمت لینا۔ خصی مرد سے خدمت لینا مکروہ ہے۔ اس طرح خصی بننے کی ہمت افزائی ہوگی۔ اس لئے خصی کئے ہوئے مرد سے خدمت لینا مکروہ ہے (۲) حدیث میں خصی کروانے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال نهى رسول الله الي الله عن اخصاء الخيل والبهائم وقال ابن عمر فيها نماء الخلق (الف) ( مسنداحمد ، سند عبد اللہ بن عمر ، ج ثانی ص ۱۰۱ نمبر ۴۷۵۵) مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ما قالوافی خصاء الخيل والدواب من كرهه ، ج سادس ص ۲۲۶، نمبر ۳۲۵۶۷) اس حدیث میں خصی کرنے سے منع فرمایا اس لئے خصیوں سے خدمت لینا مکروہ ہے۔
[۳۱۱۵) (۱۵) کوئی حرج نہیں ہے جانوروں کو خصی کرنے میں اور گدھے کوگھوڑی پر ڈالنے میں ۔ اوپر گزرا کہ جانور کو خصی کرنے میں نسل کشی ہوگی اس لئے یہ ممنوع ہے۔ لیکن بکرے کو خصی نہ کرے تو وہ موٹا نہیں ہوتا اور گوشت اچھا نہیں ہوتا۔ اس کے علاوہ وہ شرارت بہت کرتا ہے اس لئے اس کو خصی کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح بیل کو خصی نہ کرے تو وہ طاقتور نہیں ہوتا اور ہل جو تنے کے قابل نہیں ہوتا ( میں خود کسان ہوں مجھے اس کا تجربہ ہے ) اس لئے اس کو بھی خصی کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں۔ البتہ بعض کو سانڈھ ہونے کے لئے چوڑ دیا جائے تا کہ نسل ختم نہ ہو۔ حضور نے خصی بکرے کی قربانی کی ہے جس سے اندازہ ہوتا ہے کہ خصی کرنا جائز ہے ورنہ آپ خصی کی قربانی نہ کرتے ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله قال ذبح النبي الله يوم الذبح كبشين اقرنین املحین موجئين (ب) ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما يستحب من الضحايا ، ج ۲، ص ۲۰، نمبر ۲۷۹۵ رابن ماجه شریف، باب اضاحی رسول الله الله ، ص ۴۵۵، نمبر ۳۱۲۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے خصی کئے ہوئے دو بکرے ذبح فرمائے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ بعض جانور کو خصی کرنا جائز ہے۔ موجین کے معنی خصی (۲) اثر میں ہی۔ عن الحسن قال لابأس بخصاء الدواب (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۸ ، من رخص في خصاء الدواب، ج سادس، ص ۴۲۶، نمبر ۳۲۵۷۹) اپنے طور پر گدھے کو گھوڑی پر چڑھا کر خچر پیدا کروانا شریف آدمی کے لئے اچھا عمل نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اگر گدھا اور گھوڑی ایسا کر لیں اور خچر پیدا ہو جائے تو جائز ہے۔
اپنے طور پر گدھے کوگھوڑی پر چڑھانا اچھا عمل نہیں ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان رسول الله الله عبدا مامورا ما اختصنا دون الناس بشيء الا بثلاث امرنا ان نسبغ الوضوء ، وان لا ناكل الصدقة، وان لا ننزى حمارا حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے گھوڑے اور جانوروں کو خصی کرنے سے منع فرمایا، ابن عمر فر ماتے ہیں کہ ایسانہ کرنے سے مخلوق کی بڑھوتری ہے (ب) حضور نے بقرہ عید کے دن دو مینڈھے ذبح کئے جو سینگ والے چتکبرے اور نھی تھے (ج) حضرت حسن نے فرمایا چوپائے کے خصی کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
114 (14) And it is disliked to use eunuchs (as servants). [153115] And there is no harm in castrating animals and mating donkeys upon horses.
(13114 (14) It is disliked to take service from a eunuch. Taking service from a castrated man is disliked because it encourages castration. Therefore, it is disliked to take service from a castrated man. (2) In a hadith, prohibition of castration is mentioned: from Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah prohibited castration of horses and animals, and Ibn 'Umar said: 'In that (not castrating) is the growth of creation.' (a) (Musnad Ahmad, ...) In this hadith castration is prohibited, so taking service from eunuchs is disliked.
[3115) (15) There is no harm in castrating animals and in putting the donkey upon the mare. It passed earlier that castrating animals causes extinction of species, so it is prohibited. But if a goat is not castrated, it does not become fat and its meat is not good. Besides, it causes much trouble. So there is no harm in castrating it. Similarly, if a bull is not castrated, it does not become strong and is not fit for ploughing (I am a farmer myself, I have experience). So there is no harm in castrating it either. However, some should be left for breeding so that the species does not become extinct. The Messenger sacrificed a castrated ram, which indicates that castration is permissible, else he would not have sacrificed it. The hadith: from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah that the Prophet sacrificed on the day of sacrifice two horned, white-spotted, castrated rams. (b) (Abu Dawud, ...) This hadith shows that the Prophet sacrificed castrated rams, so castration of some animals is permissible. 'Mujayyeen' means castrated. (2) In an athar: from al-Hasan: he said, 'There is no harm in castrating animals.' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ...) Deliberately putting a donkey upon a mare to produce a mule is not a good practice for a noble person. However, if the donkey and mare do it themselves and a mule is born, it is permissible.
Deliberately putting a donkey upon a mare is not a good practice. Its proof is this hadith: from Ibn 'Abbas that the Messenger of Allah was a commanded servant, and he did not single us out from people except with three things: he commanded us to perform wudu thoroughly, not to eat sadaqah, and not to mate a donkey (with a mare).
Footnote: (a) The Messenger prohibited castration of horses and animals; Ibn 'Umar says that not doing so allows the growth of creation. (b) The Messenger sacrificed on the day of Eid two rams that were horned, white-spotted, and castrated. (c) Hadrat Hasan said: There is no harm in castrating cattle.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage covers two related but distinct rulings. First, employing eunuchs (castrated men) as servants is disliked (makruh) because it indirectly encourages the act of castration, which is prohibited for humans. The proof is the hadith prohibiting castration of animals, extended to humans by analogy. Second, regarding animals: castration is generally prohibited but there are exceptions. The text explains that while castration may prevent breeding, it is permissible for goats (to improve meat quality and reduce aggression) and for bulls (to make them stronger for ploughing). The proof is that the Prophet sacrificed castrated rams, showing it is allowed. However, some animals should be left intact to maintain the species. As for crossbreeding donkeys with horses to produce mules, the text says deliberate mating is not a good practice (disliked), but if it happens spontaneously, it is permissible. The hadith from Ibn 'Abbas mentions that among the things the Prophet prohibited was mating a donkey (with a mare). Therefore, actively initiating such crossbreeding is disliked, though accidental occurrence is acceptable.

Key Terms
الخصيان (al-khusyan): Castrated males, eunuchs, especially used as servants

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is employing a eunuch disliked in the Hanafi school according to this passage?
A) Eunuchs are considered ritually impure.
B) It encourages the prohibited act of castration.
C) There is no valid reason.
D) It is only disliked for Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Employing a eunuch is disliked because it implicitly supports the prohibited act of castration.

Ruling on Castrating Animals
Ruling on animal castration with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that castrating animals for benefit is permissible, and identify the conditions for its permissibility.

Core Idea
Castrating animals for valid benefit (meat, labour) is permissible despite the general prohibition.

This passage addresses the Hanafi ruling on castrating animals. While there is a general prohibition on castration from a hadith, the school makes exceptions for animals used for food or labour, based on the Prophet's own practice. Understanding this ruling demonstrates the Hanafi method of balancing primary texts with practical needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is castrating animals, specifically goats and bulls for benefit.
2
Note the general ruling
Generally, castration is prohibited because it prevents breeding and may lead to extinction.
The text references a hadith prohibiting castration of animals.
3
Recognize the exception
Castration is permissible when there is a clear benefit, such as improving meat quality (goats) or making animals stronger for work (bulls).
The condition is that some animals must be left intact for breeding.
4
Cite the proof
The Prophet sacrificed castrated rams on Eid, indicating that castration is permissible. An athar from Hasan al-Basri also states no harm.
This overrides the general prohibition via istihsan.
5
Understand the condition
To prevent extinction, not all animals should be castrated; some must be kept for breeding.

Ruling on Deliberate Crossbreeding
Ruling on deliberate crossbreeding with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that deliberate mating of a donkey with a mare is makruh tanzihi, while accidental mating is permissible.

Core Idea
Deliberately breeding mules is disliked; accidental breeding is allowed.

This passage covers the ruling on crossbreeding donkeys and horses to produce mules. The Hanafi school holds that deliberately initiating such mating is disliked (makruh tanzihi) based on a hadith of Ibn 'Abbas, but if it happens accidentally, it is permissible. This ruling reflects the Hanafi principle of discouraging actions that are not clearly beneficial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is deliberately mating a donkey with a mare to produce a mule.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful).
The text says it is 'not a good practice'.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas where the Prophet prohibited mating a donkey (with a mare).
The hadith is among three exclusive commands.
4
Distinguish intentional vs. accidental
If the mating occurs naturally without human intervention, it is permissible (mubah).
The text explicitly states this.
5
Note the practical implication
One should not actively seek to produce mules, but if it happens, no sin.

Source Text
