حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے عبداللہ بن ابی اوفی سے پوچھا کیا حضور نے وصیت کی تھی؟ فرمایا نہیں۔ میں نے کہا لوگوں پر وصیت کیسے فرض کی گئی یا اس کا حکم دیا گیا؟ فرمایا کتاب اللہ کو پکڑے رہنے کی وصیت کی (ب) آپ نے فرمایا اللہ نے تم پر صدقہ کیا ہے تمہاری وفات کے وقت تمہارے تہائی مال کا تمہارے اعمال میں زیادتی کے لئے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا کسی آدمی کے حق کے بارے میں وصیت لکھنی ہو تو دورات بھی نہیں گزارنی چاہئے کہ اس کے پاس وصیت لکھی ہوئی ہونی چاہئے۔
139 (2) The bequest for an heir is not valid unless the other heirs permit it.
Heirs already receive their share. Now, making a bequest to others and gifting wealth is something given, and giving gifts is recommended, so the bequest is also recommended. (2) In a hadith, the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not make a bequest. If making a bequest were obligatory, he would have done so. This indicates that making a bequest is recommended. The hadith: "I asked 'Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: 'Did the Prophet (peace be upon him) make a bequest?' He said, 'No.' I said, 'How was the bequest prescribed for the people or were they commanded to do it?' He said, 'He bequeathed the Book of Allah.'" (Bukhari, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawud). From this hadith, it is understood that the Prophet bequeathed adherence to the Book of Allah, not wealth. Thus, making a bequest is not obligatory. (3) In another hadith, a bequest is considered charity, and giving charity is recommended. Therefore, making a bequest is also recommended. The hadith: From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Indeed, Allah has given you charity at the time of your death, one-third of your wealth, as an increase for your deeds." (Ibn Majah). In this hadith, Allah has given you charity of bequeathing one-third of wealth, and giving charity is recommended, so the bequest is also recommended.
If a person has debt or a trust that must be fulfilled, then making a bequest for that is obligatory.
There is emphasis on this in a hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) who said: "It is not right for a Muslim who has something to bequeath that he passes two nights without having a written bequest with him." (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah). In this hadith, if there is something to bequeath, one should not delay even two nights; rather, a written bequest should be prepared. This indicates that if one has a trust or debt to pay, he should write a bequest; such a bequest is obligatory.
3139 (2) A bequest for an heir is not valid unless the other heirs give permission.
At the beginning of Islam, a bequest for heirs was obligatory. Later, the Qur'an determined the shares of all heirs, so that (obligation) was abrogated. Now, making a bequest for an heir is not permissible, because it would give more to some heirs and less to those entitled. However, if the remaining heirs give permission to execute this bequest, it will be implemented.
Formerly, making a bequest for heirs was obligatory; its evidence is this verse: "Prescribed for you, when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth..."
Footnote: (a) I asked 'Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa... (b) The Prophet said: Allah gave you charity... (c) The Prophet said: It is not right for a man...
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with explanation regarding bequests to legal heirs. The base ruling is: a bequest to an heir is not permissible unless the other heirs give their consent after the testator's death. The commentary explains the historical development: initially, bequests for heirs were obligatory through the verse al-Baqarah 2:180, but this was abrogated by the detailed inheritance verses (Ayat al-Mirath) that fixed the shares of each heir. Therefore, any bequest that gives extra to a heir is invalid because it disrupts the divinely ordained distribution. However, the ruling includes an exception: if all other heirs (the ones who would otherwise receive less) voluntarily agree to enforce the bequest after the testator's death, it becomes valid. This is because the right to object belongs to the living heirs; if they forgo their right, the bequest is implemented.
The commentary also reiterates the general ruling on the status of bequest (mustahabb) and the exception for debts/trusts, linking it to the discussion. It provides hadith evidence to support the non-obligatory nature of wasiyya and the obligation in case of debts. The footnote clarifies the hadith cited.

Key Terms
الوارث (al-warith): A person entitled to a fixed share of the deceased's estate under Islamic inheritance law.
اجازة (ijazah): Permission given by the heirs after the testator's death to enforce a bequest that would otherwise be invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always valid if it does not exceed one-third of the estate.
B) Only if the testator declares it in writing.
C) Only if all other heirs give their permission after the testator's death.
D) It is never valid under any circumstances.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a legal heir is invalid without the consent of all other heirs, because the Quranic inheritance shares are fixed.

Ruling on Lifetime Acceptance/Rejection and Recommendation to Will Less Than One-Third
Ruling with proof on invalidity of lifetime acceptance/rejection and recommendation of less than one-third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of acceptance/rejection of a will during the testator's lifetime and explain why it is recommended to will less than one-third.

Core Idea
A will becomes operative only after death; acceptance/rejection during life is void, and it is recommended to will less than one-third.

This lesson examines two key rulings from the chapter of wasiyya. First, the acceptance or rejection of a will by the legatee during the testator's lifetime has no legal effect — the will only becomes enforceable after death. Second, while one-third of the estate is the maximum that can be willed without heirs' consent, the Prophet indicated that even one-third is a substantial amount; thus it is recommended to will less than one-third, especially if the heirs are poor. We will explore the evidence from hadith and athar that support these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the nature of wasiyya
Recognize that a will is a transfer of ownership effective after death; thus the legatee's right to accept or reject only arises after death.
This is the basis for the first ruling.
2
Analyze the first ruling: lifetime acceptance/rejection is void
The matn states that acceptance/rejection during life is batil. Find the supporting athar (e.g., Umar's letter, Shurayh's ruling, the hadith of Abu Qatada) and understand why they prove that the effective time for acceptance/rejection is after death.
Key point: the legatee becomes owner only upon death.
3
Identify the second ruling and its evidence
The matn says it is mustahabb to will less than one-third. Examine the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and the athar of Ibn Abbas. Note the Prophet's wording 'one-third is much' and the permission for one-third.
The recommendation is derived from the Prophet's comment and Ibn Abbas's wish for one-fourth.
4
Apply to a practical situation
Consider a testator with poor relatives. How should he decide the amount? The recommended amount is less than one-third, e.g., one-fourth, to balance bequest and heir welfare.
This demonstrates the wisdom behind the recommendation.

Acceptance or rejection during life is invalid. [3144] (7) And it is recommended that a person make a will for less than one-third. ... [explanation and proofs] ... (13144 (7) It is recommended that a person make a will for less than one-third. The hadith says that one-third is a lot, so it is better to will less than one-third, especially if the heirs are poor. ... This hadith and athar show that it is recommended to will less than one-third, up to one-fourth.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings from the chapter of wills (wasiyya). First, the matn states that if a testator accepts or rejects a will during his own lifetime, such acceptance or rejection is void (batil). The commentator explains that the will is only established after death; the legatee becomes owner only at that point, so any expression of acceptance or rejection before death has no legal effect. This is supported by several athar (traditions) from the Companions: 1) Ibn Abi Rabi'a wrote to Umar ibn al-Khattab asking about a person who makes one will then another; Umar replied that the later one is binding. 2) Shurayh ruled that if a testator seeks permission from heirs to exceed the one-third limit and they agree, but then after burial they change their minds, they may withdraw their consent. This shows that the effective time for acceptance/rejection is after death. 3) The Prophet (peace be upon him) rejected a bequest made to him and returned it to the testator's heirs, indicating that the legatee's right to accept or reject arises only after death. The second ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended) to will less than one-third of one's estate. The hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas reports that when he wanted to will half, the Prophet said half is too much; when he suggested one-third, the Prophet said one-third is still a lot, but permitted it. Ibn Abbas wished people would will only one-fourth, since the Prophet called one-third 'a lot'. Thus the recommended amount is less than one-third, such as one-fourth or less, especially if the heirs are in need.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyya): A bequest or will, a transfer of ownership effective after the testator's death without exchange of consideration.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum amount that can be willed without heirs' consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the recommended amount to will in one's will?
A) One-half of the estate
B) One-third of the estate
C) Less than one-third of the estate
D) The entire estate

Key Takeaway
A will only takes effect after death, so acceptance/rejection during life is invalid, and it is recommended to will less than one-third of one's estate.

Ruling on Rejection of a Will in Presence vs Absence
Ruling on validity of rejecting a will in presence vs absence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a legatee's rejection of a will when done in the testator's presence versus absence, and explain the underlying rationale using the analogy of a sale contract.

Core Idea
A legatee's rejection is only effective if made in the testator's presence or with his knowledge during his lifetime.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the rejection of a will (al-wasiyyah). The key question: after a legatee has accepted the will in the testator's presence, can he later reject it silently or after the testator's death? The passage clarifies that the testator's awareness is crucial, drawing an analogy to the binding nature of a sale contract after acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that the act being ruled upon is the legatee's rejection (radd) of the will after having accepted it in the testator's presence. The passage gives two scenarios: rejection in the testator's presence (valid) and rejection in his absence without notification (invalid).
The ruling hinges on whether the testator is aware of the rejection during his lifetime.
2
Distinguish presence vs absence
In the presence of the testator (fi wajhihi), the rejection is explicit and the testator can act accordingly. In absence (ghayr wajh), if the legatee does not inform the testator, the testator dies believing the will is still in effect. Thus, the rejection is ineffective.
The term 'wajh' in this context means 'presence'.
3
Note the underlying principle
Once the will is accepted in the testator's presence, it becomes binding (like a gift or sale). To retract, the testator must be informed so he can dispose of the property elsewhere (e.g., give it in charity). Without notification, the property remains with the legatee.
The principle ensures the testator's will (in both senses) is honored.
4
Apply the qiyas analogy
The commentator draws an analogy to a sale contract: after acceptance, the sale is binding; any cancellation must be done face-to-face or with the other party's knowledge. Similarly, rejection of a will requires the testator's awareness.
The illa (effective cause) is the need for mutual awareness in binding transfers.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that rejection of a will is only effective if it takes place in the testator's presence or if the testator is informed during his lifetime. A posthumous rejection or silent rejection in absence is invalid.
This is the established ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

[۱۳۱۴۵ (۸) واذا اوصى الى رجل فقبل الوصية في وجه الموصى وردّها في غير وجهه فليس برد وان ردّها في وجهه فهو رد. وصیت کرنے والے نے وصیت کی اور جس کے لئے وصیت کی اس نے اس کے سامنے قبول کر لیا تو وصیت کی ہوگی۔ اب اگر رد کرنا چاہے تو میت کے سامنے رو کر دے یا کم از کم اس کی زندگی میں رد کرنے کی خبر بھجوادے کہ میں اس مال کو قبول نہیں کرتا ہوں تو وصیت رد ہوگی۔ اور مال میت کے ورثہ میں تقسیم ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر میت کے سامنے رو نہیں کی اور نہ اس کی زندگی میں خبر بھجوائی بلکہ اس کے مرنے کے بعد رد کی یا اس کی زندگی میں رد کی لیکن غائبانہ میں رد کی اور میت کو خبر نہیں بھجوائی تو وصیت رو نہیں ہوگی بلکہ وہ مال موصی لہ کی ملیکت میں داخل ہو جائیگا۔ یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ موصی لہ کے قبول کرنے کے بعد وصیت کی ہو گئی۔ اب اس کو توڑنا ہو تو وصیت کرنے والے کے سامنے توڑے یا اس کو خبر بھجوادے تاکہ زندگی میں اس کو اطمینان ہو جائے۔ یہ مال میرے پاس واپس آ گیا ہے۔ اب اس کو کسی اور غریب پر صدقہ کر کے دنیا سے جاتا ہے۔ اور یہ خبر نہیں پہنچی تو وہ یہ اطمینان کر کے جائے گا کہ مال ٹھکانے پہنچ چکا ہے (۲) جس طرح بیچ میں قبول کرنے کے بعد پکی ہو جاتی ہی اب اس کو توڑنا ہو تو سامنے آکر توڑے یا اس کی خبر پہنچائے۔
And if a person makes a will to a man, and that man accepts the will in the presence of the testator and rejects it in his absence, then it is not a valid rejection. But if he rejects it in his presence, then it is a rejection. [Commentary: ...]
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on how a legatee's rejection of a will is to be considered. The matn says: if the legatee accepts the will in the presence of the testator, then later rejects it in his absence (i.e., without informing the testator), that rejection is not valid. However, if he rejects it in the testator's presence, it is a valid rejection. The commentator explains the reasoning: once the legatee has accepted in the testator's presence, the will is confirmed. If he wishes to retract, he must do so in the testator's presence or at least send a message during the testator's lifetime so that the testator knows the wealth is returned and can dispose of it (e.g., give it in charity). Without such notification, the testator dies thinking the will is in effect, so the property remains with the legatee. The commentator analogizes this to a sale: after acceptance, a sale is binding; any cancellation must be done face-to-face or with knowledge of the other party. Thus, a rejection in absence without informing is ineffective.

Key Terms
وجه (wajh): Presence, in the presence of the testator.
رد (radd): Rejection or cancellation of the will by the legatee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A legatee accepts a will in the testator's presence, then later says 'I reject it' in the testator's absence without informing him. What is the ruling?
A) The will is void because he rejected it
B) The rejection is valid because he changed his mind
C) The rejection is invalid; the will remains effective
D) The rejection is valid only if he tells the heirs

Key Takeaway
A legatee's rejection of a will is effective only if the testator is made aware of it during his lifetime, either in person or through a message.

Ownership of a Bequest Requires Acceptance
Ruling on ownership transfer of a bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that ownership of a bequest requires the legatee's acceptance and explain the analogy to a sale contract.

Core Idea
A bequest is not owned until the legatee accepts it — it is a contract, not a gift.

This lesson clarifies a foundational Hanafi principle: a will does not automatically transfer ownership upon the testator's death. Instead, it functions like a sale contract, requiring the legatee's acceptance. Understanding this distinction is key to avoiding common misconceptions about inheritance and bequests.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The passage asserts that the bequeathed property (musa bihi) is owned by acceptance (qabul). The legatee must accept after the testator's death to become owner.
This is a concise rule; note the absolute phrasing.
2
Understand the analogy to sale
The commentator compares a will to a sale: in a sale, the buyer's acceptance transfers ownership; similarly, in a will, the legatee's acceptance is necessary.
The analogy highlights that a will is a bilateral contract in Hanafi law.
3
Identify the consequence of non-acceptance
If the legatee does not accept, the property does not enter his ownership; it remains part of the estate.
This differs from a gift, which is immediately binding upon offer.
4
Contrast with other schools
The Shafi'i school holds that a will is unilateral and ownership vests immediately at death unless the legatee rejects. The Hanafi requirement of acceptance is distinctive.
This ikhtilaf affects practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۱۴۶ (۹) والموطی به یملک بالقبول. وصیت کرنے والے نے وصیت کی اور جس کے لئے وصیت کی اس نے قبول کر لیا تو وصیت کی چیز موصی لہ کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو کی قبول تو کی جائے گی۔ اور قبول نہیں کیا تو اس کی ملکیت میں داخل نہیں ہوگی۔ حنفیہ کے یہاں وصیت بیچ کی طرح ہے۔ جس طرح بیچ میں بائع ایجاب کرے پھر مشتری قبول کرے تب مبیع مشتری کی ملکیت میں داخل
And the bequeathed property is owned by acceptance. [Commentary:] The testator made a will, and the person for whom it was made accepted, then the bequeathed property enters the ownership of the legatee. And if he did not accept, then it does not enter his ownership. According to the Hanafis, a will is like a sale. Just as in sale, the seller makes an offer and then the buyer accepts, then the sold item enters the ownership of the buyer.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This concise ruling establishes a fundamental principle of Hanafi wil law: the legatee (musa lahu) does not automatically become owner of the bequeathed property upon the testator's death. Rather, ownership is contingent upon his acceptance. If he accepts, he owns it; if he rejects or remains silent, he does not. The commentator analogizes a will to a sale contract: in a sale, ownership transfers only when the buyer accepts the seller's offer. Similarly, a will is an offer made by the testator that requires the legatee's acceptance to become binding. This is a distinctive feature of the Hanafi school, which treats the will as a contract rather than a unilateral disposition. The acceptance must occur after the testator's death, as established in earlier passages.

Key Terms
موصى به (musa bihi): The property or thing that is bequeathed in the will.
قبول (qabul): Acceptance by the legatee after the testator's death, which completes the transfer of ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, when does a legatee become the owner of the bequeathed property?
A) Immediately upon the testator's death
B) Upon the testator's death if he does not reject
C) Only after he accepts the will after the testator's death
D) Only if the heirs consent

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest is owned only when the legatee explicitly accepts it after the testator's death; acceptance is a necessary pillar of the will contract.

Validity of Rejection of a Will: Presence or Notice Required
Ruling on validity of rejection of a will based on presence/absence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid rejection of a will and apply it to scenarios of presence versus absence of the testator.

Core Idea
Rejection of a will is only effective if done in the testator's presence or with notice during his lifetime.

This lesson clarifies a key procedural rule in the Hanafi law of wills: when can a legatee reject a bequest? The passage establishes that acceptance makes the bequest binding; to undo it, the legatee must reject in the testator's presence or inform him. Absent rejection without notice is ineffective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
The act under consideration is the rejection of a will (radd al-wasiyyah) by the legatee after acceptance.
Rejection occurs after a valid bequest and acceptance.
2
Determine the condition for valid rejection
The text states that rejection is only valid if done in the presence of the testator (fi wajhihi) or if the testator is informed of the rejection during his lifetime.
Presence means the testator is alive and aware of the rejection.
3
Apply to scenarios
If rejection occurs in the testator's absence without informing him, it is ineffective. The bequest remains binding and the legatee owns the property.
Even if the legatee verbally rejects, if the testator does not know, the rejection is void.
4
Understand the analogy to sale
The commentary compares this to a sale (bay'): after acceptance by both parties, the contract is binding. To rescind, both must agree or the other party must be informed.
This highlights the principle that a concluded contract requires mutual consent to undo.
5
Recognize the wisdom behind the rule
The testator needs assurance that the property has returned to him so he can dispose of it (e.g., give in charity) before death. Without notice, he dies thinking the bequest is settled.
The rule protects the testator's intention and planning.

وصیت کرنے والے نے وصیت کی اور جس کے لئے وصیت کی اس نے اس کے سامنے قبول کر لیا تو وصیت کی ہوگی۔ اب اگر رد کرنا چاہے تو میت کے سامنے رو کر دے یا کم از کم اس کی زندگی میں رد کرنے کی خبر بھجوادے کہ میں اس مال کو قبول نہیں کرتا ہوں تو وصیت رد ہوگی۔ اور مال میت کے ورثہ میں تقسیم ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر میت کے سامنے رو نہیں کی اور نہ اس کی زندگی میں خبر بھجوائی بلکہ اس کے مرنے کے بعد رد کی یا اس کی زندگی میں رد کی لیکن غائبانہ میں رد کی اور میت کو خبر نہیں بھجوائی تو وصیت رو نہیں ہوگی بلکہ وہ مال موصی لہ کی ملیکت میں داخل ہو جائیگا۔
یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ موصی لہ کے قبول کرنے کے بعد وصیت کی ہو گئی۔ اب اس کو توڑنا ہو تو وصیت کرنے والے کے سامنے توڑے یا اس کو خبر بھجوادے تاکہ زندگی میں اس کو اطمینان ہو جائے۔ یہ مال میرے پاس واپس آ گیا ہے۔ اب اس کو کسی اور غریب پر صدقہ کر کے دنیا سے جاتا ہے۔ اور یہ خبر نہیں پہنچی تو وہ یہ اطمینان کر کے جائے گا کہ مال ٹھکانے پہنچ چکا ہے (۲) جس طرح بیچ میں قبول کرنے کے بعد پکی ہو جاتی ہی اب اس کو توڑنا ہو تو سامنے آکر توڑے یا اس کی خبر پہنچائے۔

Book of Wills. [13145 (8) And if he bequeaths to a man, and he accepts the will in the presence of the testator and rejects it in his absence, it is not rejection. And if he rejects it in his presence, then it is rejection. And the one to whom bequest is made acquires ownership by acceptance. The people are limited to one-third, so that is permissible for them (a) (Bukhari, Book of Bequest of One-Third, p. 383, no. 2744). And there is an effect of Abdullah ibn Abbas: 'I wish that people would bequeath up to one-fourth.' It is an effect: from Ibn Abbas: 'If people would lower to one-fourth, because the Messenger of Allah said: one-third, and one-third is a lot' (b) (Bukhari, Book of Bequest of One-Third, p. 1383, nos. 2743/2744; Muslim, Book of Bequest of One-Third, p. 138, no. 1629; Abu Dawud, Book of What is Permissible for the Testator in His Wealth, p. 139, no. 2864; Ibn Majah, Book of Bequest of One-Third, p. 1390, no. 11(27)). From this hadith and effect it is understood that bequeathing less than one-third, up to one-fourth of wealth, is recommended. (13145 (8) If someone bequeathed to someone, then he accepted the will in the presence of the testator and rejected it in absentia, it will not be rejection. And if he rejected it in his presence, then it will be rejection. The testator made a bequest and the legatee accepted it in his presence, so the bequest is finalized. Now if he wants to reject, he should reject in the presence of the deceased or at least send news of rejection during his lifetime that 'I do not accept this property', then the will is rejected and the property is distributed among the testator's heirs. And if he did not reject in the presence of the deceased nor sent news during his lifetime, but rejected after his death or rejected during his lifetime in absentia without informing the testator, then the will is not rejected; rather, the property enters into the ownership of the legatee. This issue is based on the principle that after the legatee's acceptance, the bequest is concluded. Now if it is to be broken, it must be broken in the presence of the testator or he should send news so that he is assured during his lifetime that 'this property has returned to me, now I can give it in charity to another poor person and depart from the world.' And if the news did not reach, he will depart with the assurance that the property has reached its destination. (2) Just as in a sale, after acceptance it becomes final; if it is to be broken, one must come before the other or send news. Footnote: (a) Hadrat Sa'd says: I fell ill, and the Prophet came to visit me. I said: I want to make a will. I have only one daughter, so I bequeath half of my wealth. He said: Half is too much. I said: One-third. He said: One-third is fine, but it is also a lot. People may bequeath one-third, it is permissible for them. (b) Hadrat Ibn Abbas said: If people bequeath up to one-fourth, it is fine, because the Prophet said one-third is fine, but it is a lot.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on acceptance and rejection of a will, with commentary explaining the conditions. The ruling states that if a legatee accepts the will in the presence of the testator but rejects it in his absence, it is not considered a valid rejection. Only rejection in the presence of the testator is effective. The commentary elaborates that after acceptance, the bequest is binding; to undo it, the legatee must reject in the testator's presence or send news during his lifetime. The principle is analogous to a sale: after acceptance, the contract is final. The hadith and athar about bequeathing one-third or less are also discussed, showing that bequeathing less than one-third (such as one-fourth) is recommended.

Key Terms
موصى له (mūṣā lahu): The person to whom a bequest is made; the legatee.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest or will.
رد (radd): Rejection or revocation of a will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The rejection is valid and the property returns to the testator.
B) The rejection is not valid, and the property remains with the legatee if he had accepted.
C) The rejection is valid only if the legatee makes a new acceptance.
D) The testator must be present for any rejection to be valid.

Key Takeaway
Rejection of a will after acceptance is only effective if the testator is present or informed during his lifetime.

Ownership of a Bequest: The Requirement of Acceptance
States that legatee obtains ownership only by acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a bequest transfers ownership only upon the legatee's acceptance and explain the analogy to a sale.

Core Idea
A bequest is like a sale: ownership passes only with acceptance.

This lesson focuses on the fundamental Hanafi principle that a bequest does not transfer ownership automatically. Unlike inheritance, which vests immediately, a bequest requires the legatee's explicit acceptance. The passage compares a bequest to a sale, where both offer and acceptance are necessary for the contract to be effective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The legatee must accept the bequest for ownership to transfer.
2
Understand the analogy
Just as a sale requires both offer and acceptance, so does a bequest.
The Hanafis liken bequest to a sale because both are contracts of transfer.
3
Consider the evidence
The athar from al-Sha'bi and Ibn 'Awn support this requirement.
Al-Sha'bi: 'No bequest for a dead person' – death renders acceptance impossible. Ibn 'Awn: commanded to accept the bequest, showing acceptance is necessary.

۳۱۴۶ (۹) والموطی به یملک بالقبول.
وصیت کرنے والے نے وصیت کی اور جس کے لئے وصیت کی اس نے قبول کر لیا تو وصیت کی چیز موصی لہ کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو کی قبول تو کی جائے گی۔ اور قبول نہیں کیا تو اس کی ملکیت میں داخل نہیں ہوگی۔
حنفیہ کے یہاں وصیت بیچ کی طرح ہے۔ جس طرح بیچ میں بائع ایجاب کرے پھر مشتری قبول کرے تب مبیع مشتری کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جاتی ہے۔ اسی طرح وصیت میں موصی وصیت کرے اور موصی لہ اس کو قبول کرے تب وصیت کی چیز موصیلہ کی ملکیت میں داخل ہوگی۔ اور اگر موصی لہ نے انکار کر دیا یا اس کو خبر پہنچی اور وہ خاموش رہا تو وصیت کی چیز اس کی ملکیت نہیں ہوگی۔ موصی لہ کے قبول کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے که وصیت ایک قسم کا احسان ہے تو ممکن ہے کہ موصی لہ اس احسان کو نہ لینا چاہتا ہو۔ یا وہ مثلا فقیر نہیں ہے اور موسی صدقے کے مال کی وصیت موصی لہ کے لئے کرنا چاہتا ہے جس کی وجہ سے موصی لہ اس کے حق میں ہے کہ صدقے کا مال میں نہ لوں ۔ اس لئے وہ قبول کرے گا تو ملکیت ہوگی ورنہ نہیں (۱) اس اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن الشعبي قال لا وصية لميت (الف ) ( مصنف ابن ابی شبیة ، الرجل يومى لرجل بوصیتہ فیموت الموصی له قبل اموصی ، ج سادس، ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۳۰۷۳۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جو مر چکا ہے اس کے لئے وصیت کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ وصیت کی چیز کو قبول کرنے کا اہل نہیں رہا۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وصیت کی چیز کو قبول کرنے سے موصی لہ کی ملکیت ہوگی (۲) یہ اثر بھی اس کی دلیل ہے۔ عن ابن عون قال اوصى الى ابن عم فكرهت ذلك فسألت عمرا فامرني ان اقبلها قال وكان ابن سيرين يقبل الوصية (ب) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ۴۵ فی قبول الوصیة من کان یومی الی الرجل فيقبل ذلك، ج سادس ص ۲۲۷، نمبر ۳۰۹۰۱) اس میں وصیت قبول کی تب وصی بنا۔ فانده امام شافعی اور امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح وراثت بغیر وارثین کے قبول کے میت کے مرتے ہی اس کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جاتی ہے۔ اسی طرح وصیت کی چیز بغیر موصی لہ کے قبول کئے اس کی ملکیت میں داخل ہو جائے گی۔
[13146] (9) And the one to whom bequest is made acquires ownership by acceptance. The testator made a bequest and the legatee accepted, so the bequeathed property enters the ownership of the legatee. And if he did not accept, it does not enter his ownership. According to the Hanafis, a bequest is like a sale. Just as in a sale, the seller makes an offer, then the buyer accepts, then the sold item enters the buyer's ownership, similarly in a bequest, the testator bequeaths and the legatee accepts, then the bequeathed property enters the legatee's ownership. And if the legatee rejects or is informed and remains silent, the bequeathed property does not become his ownership. The need for the legatee's acceptance is because a bequest is a type of favor; it is possible that the legatee does not want to accept the favor, or he is not poor and the testator wants to bequeath charity property to him, so the legatee may not want to take charity property. Therefore, if he accepts, ownership occurs; otherwise not. (1) There is an indication of this in the athar: from al-Sha'bi: 'There is no bequest for a dead person' (a) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter: a person bequeaths to a man and the legatee dies before the testator, vol. 6, p. 211, no. 30732). This athar states that a bequest for one who has died is not valid because he is not capable of acceptance, showing that acceptance by the legatee is needed for ownership. (2) Another athar supports this: from Ibn 'Awn: 'My cousin bequeathed to me, and I disliked it, so I asked 'Amr, and he commanded me to accept it. He said: Ibn Sirin used to accept bequests' (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on acceptance of bequest, vol. 6, p. 227, no. 30901). This shows that after acceptance, he became the executor. So Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar say: Just as inheritance enters the heirs' ownership upon the deceased's death without their acceptance, similarly the bequeathed property enters the legatee's ownership without acceptance.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the necessity of acceptance for ownership of a bequest. The ruling states that the legatee acquires ownership only by acceptance. The commentary elaborates that the Hanafi view likens a bequest to a sale: both require acceptance for ownership transfer. The reason is that a bequest is a gift-like favor; the legatee may not want it. Evidence is provided from athar: al-Sha'bi's statement that a bequest to a dead person is invalid because they cannot accept, and Ibn 'Awn's narration where he was commanded to accept. The opposing view of al-Shafi'i and Zufar is mentioned: they analogize bequest to inheritance, where ownership transfers automatically without acceptance. The Hanafi position is therefore established.

Key Terms
موصى به (mūṣā bihi): The property or object that is bequeathed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the legatee become the owner of a bequeathed property?
A) Immediately upon the testator's death.
B) Only after the legatee accepts the bequest.
C) Upon the testator's making the will.
D) After the court approves the will.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest requires the legatee's acceptance to transfer ownership, just as a sale requires the buyer's acceptance.

The Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Zufar Dispute on Bequest Acceptance
Presents the inter-madhab dispute on acceptance requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i/Zufar positions on whether a bequest requires acceptance for ownership and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Bequest is not inheritance; the legatee must accept the favor.

This lesson examines the scholarly disagreement between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i/Zufar on the role of acceptance in bequests. The Hanafis require acceptance, analogizing bequest to a sale, while the Shafi'is and Zufar compare it to inheritance, where ownership transfers automatically. We explore each side's evidence and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Acceptance is necessary for ownership transfer.
The Hanafis base this on direct textual evidence and the contractual nature of bequest.
2
Identify the opposing position
Ownership transfers automatically without acceptance.
Shafi'i and Zufar analogize bequest to inheritance.
3
Analyze the proofs
Hanafi relies on athar (e.g., 'no bequest for a dead person'); Shafi'i uses qiyas to inheritance.
Which evidence is more direct? The Hanafi evidence is textual, while the Shafi'i is analogical.
4
Determine the practical difference
If the legatee dies before accepting, Hanafi: bequest fails; Shafi'i: bequest passes to legatee's heirs.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text

6 min
Acceptance of Bequest Upon Legatee's Death
Ruling on implicit acceptance of bequest when legatee dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a bequest is presumed accepted upon the testator's death and apply it when the legatee dies before explicit acceptance.

Core Idea
A bequest is presumed accepted; the legatee's death does not void it.

In Hanafi law, a bequest (wasiyyah) transfers ownership to the legatee upon the testator's death. But what if the legatee dies before explicitly accepting? This lesson examines the ruling that acceptance is presumed, so the bequest enters the legatee's estate and passes to his heirs. Understanding this presumption is key to applying wasiyyah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the acceptance of a bequest. The ruling: if the legatee dies without explicit acceptance, the bequest is considered accepted and becomes part of his estate.
The default is acceptance, not rejection.
2
Understand the basis
The testator's will effectively transfers ownership from his side. The legatee's lack of rejection implies acceptance, as a beneficial gift is normally accepted.
Formal acceptance is not required if the legatee is alive but unaware.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Suppose a testator wills a house to Zaid. Zaid dies after the testator but before saying 'I accept'. The house becomes part of Zaid's estate and goes to his heirs.
The result is the same as if Zaid had explicitly accepted before death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القبول فيدخل الموصى به فى ملك ورثته موصی لہ مر گیا تو یہ مال موصی لہ کے ورثہ کی ملکیت ہو جائے گی (۲) موصی نے وصیت کر دی تو اپنی جانب سے مال موصی لہ کی ملکیت میں داخل کر دی۔ اب موصی لہ زندہ تو تھا لیکن خبر نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے قبول یا انکار نہ کر سکا تو ظاہری حال یہی ہے کہ وہ قبول ہی کرے گا۔ اس لئے اس کی ملکیت میں داخل شمار کر کے اس کے ورثہ میں تقسیم ہو جائے گا۔ اس صورت میں موصی لہ کا با ضابطہ قبول کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ الموصى : اسم فاعل کا صیغہ ہے وصیت کرنے والا، الموصی لہ: جس کے لئے وصیت کی، الموصی بہ : جس مال کی وصیت کی۔
Acceptance: So the bequeathed item enters into the ownership of his heirs. If the legatee died, this property becomes the ownership of the legatee's heirs (2) The testator made a will, so from his side he entered the property into the ownership of the legatee. Now if the legatee was alive but due to lack of news he could not accept or reject, then the apparent situation is that he would accept. Therefore, it is counted as having entered his ownership and will be distributed among his heirs. In this case, the legatee's formal acceptance is no longer necessary. Al-Musi: is the form of the active participle, the testator. Al-Musa lahu: the one for whom the will is made. Al-Musa bihi: the property for which the will is made.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on acceptance of a bequest in Hanafi law. The text states that upon the testator's death, the bequest enters the ownership of the legatee. If the legatee dies before explicitly accepting, the bequest automatically becomes part of his estate and passes to his heirs. This is because the default assumption is that one would accept a beneficial gift. Formal acceptance is thus not required if the legatee was alive at the testator's death but unable to respond. The passage also defines key terms: al-musi (testator), al-musa lahu (legatee), and al-musa bihi (bequest property). This ruling is based on the principle that acceptance of a bequest is presumed in the absence of rejection.

Key Terms
المُوصِي (al-muṣī): The person who makes the will (testator).
المُوصَى لَهُ (al-mūṣā lahu): The person for whom the will is made (legatee).
المُوصَى بِهِ (al-mūṣā bihi): The property that is bequeathed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the legatee dies before explicitly accepting the bequest, what happens to the bequeathed property according to the passage?
A) It returns to the testator's estate.
B) It goes to the public treasury.
C) It enters the estate of the legatee by default.
D) It becomes the property of the executor.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, acceptance of a bequest is presumed, so the legatee's death does not invalidate the bequest; it passes to his heirs.

8 min
Invalidity of Appointing Slave, Disbeliever, or Sinner as Executor
Ruling that the judge must remove such executors and appoint others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of people who cannot be executors and explain the judge's duty to remove them and appoint a qualified Muslim.

Core Idea
A slave, disbeliever, or open sinner cannot be an executor; the judge must remove them and appoint a qualified Muslim.

The testator may choose anyone to execute his will, but Islamic law imposes conditions on who can serve. This passage from al-Sharh al-Saghir explains that a slave, a disbeliever (kafir), and a fasiq (open sinner) are ineligible. If appointed, the judge must remove them and appoint a suitable Muslim. We will explore the proofs from the Quran and early practice that support this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited categories
Recognize that a slave, a disbeliever (kafir), and a fasiq (open sinner) are invalid executors.
2
State the judge's obligation
The judge must remove them and appoint a fit person (free, Muslim, just).
3
Examine the proofs
The text cites a Quranic verse (4:144) against taking disbelievers as allies, and athar from Sahaba about slaves and executors.
Pay attention to the athar from Amir, Ibn Abbas, and Sufyan.
4
Understand the rationale
Slaves lack independent legal capacity; disbelievers cannot be guardians over Muslims; fasiqs are untrustworthy.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, if an executor becomes accused or falls into these categories, the judge intervenes.
This ruling is absolute — no exception.

Source Text

(۱۳۱۴۸ (۱۱) و من اوصى الى عبد او كافر او فاسق اخرجهم القاضى من الوصية ونصب غيرهم. كسی نے وصیت کی غلام کو یا کافر کو یا فاسق کو تو قاضی ان کو وصیت سے نکال دے اور مقر کر دے ان کے علاوہ کو۔ غلام یا کافر یا فاسق اس لائق نہیں ہیں کہ ان کو وصی بنائے اور وصیت کے مال پر نگران بنائے۔ تاہم موصی نے بنادیا تو قاضی ان لوگوں کو وصی بننے سے نکال دے اور ان کی جگہ پر عاقل مسلمان اور عادل آدمی کو وصی مقرر کرے۔ یہ مسئلہ اس اثر سے متفرع ہے۔ عن عامر قال الوصى بمنزلة الوالد واذا اتهم الوصى عزل او جعل معه غيره (الف) مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۳۱ من قال وصیۃ العبد حیث جعلها ، ج سادس ، ص ۲۲۴، نمبر ۳۰۸۶۵ مس ف عبدالرزاق، الوصية حيث يضعها صاحبها و وصیة المعتوه و وصیة الرجل ثم يقتل والرجل یوصی بعبده - ۴۰ فی العبد یوصی اتجوز وصیته ، ج سادس، ص۲۲۴، نمبر ۳۰۸۶۳ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، الرجل یوصی لامه وهی ام ولد لا بیہ والذی یومی لعبده : ج تاسع ہیں ۹۰ نمبر ۱۶۴۶۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غلام اپنے مال کی وصیت نہیں کر سکتا تو وہ دوسرے کا وصی کیسے بنے گا ؟ کا فر کو وصی بنانا بھی صحیح نہیں۔ کونکہ وہ مسلمان کا نگران نہیں بن سکتا۔ آیت میں ہے۔ یا ایھا الذین آمنوا لا تتخذوا الكافرين اولياء من دون المؤمنين اتريدون ان تجعلواا لله عليكم سلطانا مبينا (ج) ( آیت ۱۴۴، سورة النساء۴ ) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفار کو دوست اور نگران مت بناؤ۔ اس لئے کفار وصی نہیں بن سکتا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ قال سفيان لايجوز وصية لاهل الحرب (و)(مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، ۷۹ الوصیة لاهل الحرب، ج سادس، ص ۲۴۰، نمبر ۳۱۰۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حربی کو وصی بنانا جائز نہیں۔ اور فاسق کو وصی بنانا اس لئے صحیح نہیں کہ وہ مجسم ہے۔ معلوم نہیں وصیت کے مال کو صحیح جگہ پر خرچ کرے گا یا نہیں۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ متہم ہو تو حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عامر نے فرمایا وصی والد کے درجے میں ہے اگر وصی متہم ہو گیا تو قاضی اس کو معزول کر دے یا اس کے ساتھ دوسرے کو ملا دے (ب) حضرت طہمان نے حضرت ابن عباس سے پوچھا کیا غلام وصیت کر سکتا ہے؟ فرمایا نہیں (ج) اے ایمان والو! مومنین کو چھوڑ کر کافروں کو دوست مت بناؤ۔ کیا چاہتے ہو کہ اللہ کا تم پر واضح دلیل آجائے (د) حضرت سفیان نے فرمایا حربی کے لئے وصیت نہیں ہے۔
(13148) (11) And whoever appoints as executor a slave, a disbeliever, or a sinful person, the judge removes them from the executorship and appoints others. Someone made a will appointing a slave, or a disbeliever, or a sinful person: so the judge removes them from the executorship and appoints others instead. A slave, a disbeliever, or a sinful person are not fit to be appointed as executor and overseer of the bequest property. However, if the testator appointed them, the judge removes these people from being executors and appoints in their place a sensible, Muslim, and just person as executor. This issue is derived from this athar: from Amir who said, 'The executor is in the position of the father; if the executor becomes accused, the judge removes him or appoints another with him.' (Al-Mughni ibn Abi Shayba, 31, who said the will of a slave when he makes it, vol. 6, p. 224, no. 30865; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, the will where its owner places it, and the will of an insane person, and the will of a man then he kills, and the man bequeaths his slave, vol. 9, p. 195, no. 16486). From this athar it is understood that if the executor is accused, the judge will replace him, or appoint someone else with him so that he cannot betray the bequest property. Now the situation of a slave: he cannot do any work without his master's permission, so how can he be an executor for anyone? To the extent that he cannot even make a will for his own property, so how can he be an executor for someone else? There is an athar: Tuhman asked Ibn Abbas, 'Can a slave make a will?' He said, 'No.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba - 40, concerning the slave making a will: is his will valid? vol. 6, p. 224, no. 30863; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, the man makes a will for his mother while she is an umm walad for his father, and the one who makes a will for his slave, vol. 9, p. 90, no. 16465). From this athar it is understood that a slave cannot make a will for his own property, so how can he be an executor for someone else? Appointing a disbeliever as executor is also not correct. Because he cannot be a guardian for a Muslim. In the verse: 'O you who believe! Do not take the disbelievers as allies instead of the believers. Do you wish to give Allah a clear proof against you?' (Quran 4:144). From this verse it is understood that disbelievers should not be taken as friends and guardians. Therefore, disbelievers cannot be executors. (2) There is an athar: Sufyan said, 'A will is not permissible for the people of war.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 79, the will for the people of war, vol. 6, p. 240, no. 31020). From this athar it is understood that appointing a harbi as executor is not permissible. And appointing a sinful person as executor is not correct because he is an open sinner; it is not known whether he will spend the bequest property in the right place or not. And it has already passed that if he is accused, footnote: (a) Amir said, 'The executor is in the position of the father; if the executor becomes accused, the judge removes him or appoints another with him.' (b) Tuhman asked Ibn Abbas, 'Can a slave make a will?' He said, 'No.' (c) O you who believe! Do not take the disbelievers as allies instead of the believers. Do you wish to give Allah a clear proof against you? (d) Sufyan said, 'A will is not permissible for the people of war.'
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that a slave, a disbeliever, or a sinful person (fasiq) cannot serve as an executor (wasi). The judge must remove them and appoint a qualified person. The text provides multiple proofs: (1) An athar from Amir stating that an executor is like a father, and if accused, the judge replaces him or adds another. (2) A slave cannot even make a will for himself, so he cannot be an executor. (3) The Quranic verse 4:144 prohibits taking disbelievers as guardians. (4) An athar from Sufyan forbids appointing a harbi (enemy in war). The fasiq is excluded because he is untrustworthy. The ruling is clear: the judge must intervene to ensure the will is properly executed.

Key Terms
وصي (waṣī): An executor appointed to manage the bequest and estate after death.
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who openly commits sins and is not trustworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a reason for the judge to remove an executor?
A) The executor is a slave.
B) The executor is a disbeliever.
C) The executor is an open sinner (fasiq).
D) The executor is a close relative.

Key Takeaway
A slave, kafir, or fasiq cannot be executor; the judge must replace them with a qualified Muslim to ensure the will is executed properly.

Invalidity of Appointing a Slave as Executor with Adult Heirs
Ruling on slave executorship with adult heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a slave as executor and distinguish when it is valid or invalid based on the heirs' status.

Core Idea
A slave cannot supervise a free adult; thus the appointment is invalid if any heir is adult and free.

This passage builds on the general rule that a slave cannot be an executor by examining a specific scenario: when the testator appoints his own slave as executor. The ruling depends on the composition of the heirs. If there is at least one adult free heir, the appointment is invalid because it subjects a free person to a slave's authority. However, if all heirs are minor children, necessity permits the slave to serve as executor until they come of age.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is appointing one's own slave as executor. The ruling is that it is invalid (batil) if the heirs include adults.
Note the distinction: the ruling is about the testator's own slave, not a slave belonging to someone else.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from Ibn Abbas that causing harm in a will is a major sin, linking it to Quran 4:12.
The athar is found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Appointing a slave over an adult free heir causes harm (ḍirār) because it subjects a free person to a slave's authority, which is degrading and violates the heir's rights.
The Quranic verse warns against harming the heirs.
4
Note the exception
If all heirs are minor children, a slave may be appointed as executor out of necessity, since minors cannot manage their own affairs and need a guardian.
The exception is temporary; once minors reach adulthood, the slave's executorship ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۱۴۹ (۱۲) ومن اوصى الى عبد نفسه وفى والورثة كبارٌ لم تصح الوصية میت کے ورثہ میں بالغ آدمی موجود ہے پھر بھی اپنے غلام کو وصی بنایا تو یہ اس کو وصی بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اوپر گزرا کہ غلام وصی نہیں بن سکتا۔ اور یہاں تو غلام کو وصی مان لیں تو بالغ آزاد پر اس کی نگرانی ہو جائے گی اور غلام بالغ آزاد پر نگرانی نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے غلام کو وصی بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے (۲) اس صورت میں آزاد بالغ کی حق تلفی بھی ہے کہ آزاد اور بالغ ہوتے ہوئے غلام کو وصی اور نگران بنایا۔ اس لئے غلام کو وصی بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال الضرار في الوصية من الكبار ثم تلى غير مضار وصيه من الله (الف) ( آیت ۱۲ سورۃ النسا ۴ ، مصنف ابن ابی هیبت ، ۲۷ من کان یوسی و سیستمها ، ج سادس ص ۲۲۹، نمبر ۳۰۹۲۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اولاد میں سے بھی بڑے کو وصیت کرنی چاہئے چہ جائیکہ غلام کو وصیت کرے۔ و اگر ورثہ میں صرف چھوٹے بچے ہوں تو غلام کونگران اور وصی بنا سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ چھوٹا بچہ نگرانی کیسے کرے گا۔ پھر اس کی حفاظت کون کرے گا۔ اس لئے اس مجبوری کے دور ہونے تک غلام وصی رہ سکتا ہے۔
(12) And whoever appoints his own slave as executor while the heirs are adults, the executorship is not valid. The deceased's heirs include an adult person, yet he appointed his slave as executor, so this appointment is not correct. It has passed above that a slave cannot be an executor. And here, if we accept the slave as executor, then he would be supervising a free adult, and a slave cannot supervise a free adult. Therefore, appointing a slave as executor is not correct. (2) In this case, there is also a violation of the rights of the free adult: that despite being free and adult, a slave is made executor and overseer. Therefore, appointing a slave as executor is not correct. There is an athar: from Ibn Abbas who said, 'Causing harm in a will is from the major sins.' Then he recited, 'without harming his executor from Allah' (Quran 4:12) ( Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 27, those who used to make wills and their interpretation, vol. 6, p. 229, no. 30924). From this athar it is understood that even among the children, the elder should be made executor, let alone a slave. And if the heirs are only minor children, then a slave can be made guardian and executor. Because how can a minor child supervise? Then who will protect him? Therefore, until this necessity ends, the slave can remain executor.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling that appointing one's own slave as executor is invalid when the heirs include adults. The reasoning is clear: a slave lacks the capacity to supervise a free adult; it would be disrespectful to subject a free adult to a slave's authority. The text also provides an athar from Ibn Abbas, linking this to the Quranic verse about causing harm in a will. An exception is made: if the heirs are only minor children, a slave may serve as executor out of necessity, until the children come of age.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permitted to appoint a slave as executor according to this passage?
A) When the testator has no other relatives.
B) When the heirs are all minor children.
C) When the slave is the testator's own slave.
D) It is never permitted.

Key Takeaway
Appointing a slave as executor is invalid if any heir is an adult free person; it is only valid by necessity if all heirs are minors.

Judge Appoints Co-Executor When Executor is Incapable
Ruling with proof on judge's duty for incapable executor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an appointed executor is incapable and explain the proof from the athar.

Core Idea
If the executor is incapable, the judge adds a co-executor, not replace him.

When a testator chooses an executor who turns out to be incapable, the judge faces a dilemma: respect the testator's choice or ensure the will is executed properly. The Hanafi school balances both by appointing a co-executor rather than removing the original. This lesson examines the ruling and its scriptural basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The testator appoints an executor who lacks the ability to properly execute the will.
Incapacity can be due to incompetence, illness, old age, etc.
2
State the ruling
The judge must appoint a co-executor (ضم إليه غيره) to assist the incapable one.
The ruling is wajib on the judge, not discretionary.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar from Amir: 'The executor is like a father; if accused, he is removed or another is added.'
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Incapacity is treated as a flaw similar to accusation; the judge has the option to remove or add. Here, adding preserves the testator's choice while ensuring execution.
The analogy: incapability = flaw, so the same remedy (add another) applies.
5
Note the practical effect
The original executor remains but is assisted, so the will is carried out properly.
This balances respect for the testator and the welfare of the estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۵۰) (۱۳) ومن اوصى الى من يعجز عن القيام بالوصية ضم اليه القاضي غيره کسی نے ایسے آدمی کو وصیت کی جو اس کو انجام دینے سے عاجز ہے تو قاضی اس کے ساتھ اس کے علاوہ کو شامل کر دے۔ موصی نے ایسے آدمی کو وصی بنایا جو وصیت کو کما حقہ انجام نہیں دے سکتا تو قاضی کسی اچھے آدمی کو اس کے ساتھ شامل کر دے تا کہ دھیت اچھی طرح انجام پاسکے۔ پہلے اثر گزر چکا ہے۔ عن عامر قال الوصى بمنزلة الوالد، واذا اتهم الوصى عزل او جعل معه غيره (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۴۱م من قال وصیتۃ العبد حیث جعلها ، ج سادس، ص ۲۲۴، نمبر ۳۰۸۶۵ / مصنف عبد الرزاق الوصية حيث يضعها صاحبها الخ ، ج تاسع ، ص ۹۵، نمبر ۶ (۱۶۴۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ وصی متہم ہو یا کوئی خامی ہو تو اس کو معزول کر دے یا اس کے ساتھ کسی دوسرے کو شامل کرے۔اس لئے یہاں وصیت انجام دینے سے عاجز ہے تو دوسرے کو اس کے ساتھ شامل کر دے۔ تا کہ موصی کی بات بھی رہ جائے اور وصیت بھی اچھی طرح انجام پا جائے۔
(13) And whoever appoints as executor someone who is incapable of carrying out the executorship, the judge joins another person with him. Someone appointed a person as executor who is unable to properly execute the will, so the judge adds a good person with him so that the will may be carried out well. The previous athar has passed: from Amir who said, 'The executor is in the position of the father; if the executor becomes accused, the judge removes him or appoints another with him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 41, who said the will of a slave when he makes it, vol. 6, p. 224, no. 30865; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, the will where its owner places it, etc., vol. 9, p. 95, no. 16486). In this athar it is stated that if the executor is accused or has some flaw, the judge removes him or appoints another with him. Therefore, here since he is incapable of executing the will, the judge appoints another with him, so that the testator's wish is preserved and the will is properly executed.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that if the testator appoints an executor who is incapable of fulfilling the duties, the judge must appoint a co-executor to assist him. The proof is an athar from Amir that compares the executor to a father, and if he is accused or flawed, the judge either removes him or adds another. Here, incapability is treated as a flaw, so the judge adds a capable person rather than removing the original, respecting the testator's choice. This ensures the will is executed properly.

Key Terms
عجز (ʿajz): Inability to properly execute the duties of an executor.
وصي (waṣī): Executor appointed in a will to manage the estate.
ضم (ḍamma): To join or add, here meaning to appoint a co-executor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Removes the executor and appoints a new one.
B) Appoints a co-executor to assist the incapable one.
C) Declares the will invalid.
D) Leaves the executor alone.

Key Takeaway
The judge must appoint a co-executor to assist an incapable executor, preserving both the testator's choice and proper execution.

Joint Executors: Must They Act Together?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on executor independence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on joint executors and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Two executors appointed jointly must act together; one cannot act alone according to the majority of the Hanafi school.

When a testator appoints two executors, can one of them sell property or manage the estate without the other? The Hanafi school has an internal difference. This passage presents the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, who require joint action. Understanding this helps us see how the school handles co-agency in will execution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
The passage describes a testator who appoints two persons as executors (wasi). What is the basic ruling about the authority of each executor?
The key phrase: 'لم يجز لاحدهما ان يتصرف' — it is not permissible for one of them to act.
2
Locate the difference within the Hanafi school
The text says 'عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد' — implying that this is not the unanimous Hanafi view. Who held a different opinion, and why might they differ?
The opposing view is attributed to Abu Yusuf (though not named here). His likely position: if one executor is absent or incapacitated, the other may act alone.
3
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one executor sells a property without the other, is the sale valid? According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is invalid; according to Abu Yusuf, it might be valid.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is the joint action requirement, so a judge would replace a non-cooperating executor.
4
Note the court's intervention
The Urdu gloss adds that the judge will replace the executor who acts alone and appoint another. This is the remedy when one executor refuses to cooperate or acts improperly.
This reflects the Hanafi principle that the court supervises executors to protect the estate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۵۱](۱۴) ومن اوصى الى اثنين لم يجز لاحدهما ان يتصرف عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله قاضي اس کو بدل دے گا اور اس کی جگہ دوسرے کو وصی متعین کرے گا۔
(14) And whoever appoints two executors, it is not permissible for one of them to act alone according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them. The judge will replace him and appoint another executor in his place.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage presents a brief ruling and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states that when two executors are appointed, one of them cannot act independently; they must act jointly. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The mention of 'عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد' implies that Abu Yusuf likely held a different view, allowing one executor to act alone if the other is unavailable or incapable. However, the text does not elaborate on Abu Yusuf's view. The 'mufta bihi' position is the joint action. The additional line in Urdu appears to be a marginal note about the judge replacing an executor, which may be an interpolation.

Key Terms
إثنين (ithnayn): Two executors appointed jointly.
يتصرف (yataṣarraf): To act, take action, or manage the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if two executors are appointed, can one of them act alone?
A) Yes, if the other is unavailable.
B) No, it is not permissible.
C) Only with the court's permission.
D) Yes, for minor decisions.

Key Takeaway
When two executors are appointed, the mufta bihi Hanafi position requires them to act jointly; a single executor acting alone invalidates the transaction.

Ruling on Bequest of a Share (Sahm)
Ruling on bequest of unspecified share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a testator bequeaths an unspecified 'share' (sahm) and calculate the beneficiary's portion.

Core Idea
When a testator bequeaths 'a share', the beneficiary receives the smallest heir's share, but never less than one-sixth.

This passage is a concise ruling from the matn addressing an ambiguous bequest. The word 'sahm' (share) is undefined, so the Hanafi school interprets it by reference to the actual heirs' shares, ensuring the bequest is meaningful and not trivial. The one-sixth floor is derived from common usage (urf) and prevents an unreasonably small gift.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest term
Recognize that the testator used the word 'sahm' without specifying a fraction. This triggers the default interpretation.
If the testator specified a fraction, that fraction would be used instead.
2
Determine the smallest heir's share
Calculate the shares of all legal heirs as per inheritance rules. Identify the heir with the smallest fractional share.
The smallest heir's share could be 1/8, 1/6, 1/4, etc., depending on the heir configuration.
3
Apply the one-sixth floor
If the smallest heir's share is less than one-sixth, raise it to one-sixth. Otherwise, use that share as the bequest amount.
The one-sixth floor is based on the customary meaning of 'sahm' as reported from early authorities.
4
Consider the one-third limit
Ensure the bequest does not exceed one-third of the estate unless all heirs consent. This is a general bequest rule not stated here but implied.
If the calculated share exceeds one-third, it is reduced to one-third, but that is beyond the scope of this specific ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اوطى بسهم من ماله فله اخس سهام الورثة الا ان ينقص عن السدس فيتم له السدس
And whoever bequeaths a share (sahm) of his property, he gets the smallest heir's share unless it falls short of one-sixth, then one-sixth is completed for him.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This is a ruling about an undefined bequest using the word 'sahm' (share). The Hanafi school holds that when a testator says 'I bequeath a share of my property' without specifying the fraction, the beneficiary receives the smallest share among the legal heirs. However, if that smallest share is less than one-sixth, it is raised to one-sixth because 'sahm' in Arab usage customarily means one-sixth (as supported by the athar of Ata). Additionally, the share cannot exceed one-third of the total estate because bequests beyond one-third require heirs' permission. The ruling ensures the bequest is not less than the typical understanding of a share.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): An unspecified share, interpreted as the smallest heir's share or one-sixth.
اخس (akhas): Smallest or least, referring to the heir with the smallest share.
سدس (sudus): One-sixth, the minimum floor for the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths 'a share' of his property, and the smallest heir's share is one-eighth, how much does the beneficiary receive?
A) One-eighth
B) One-sixth
C) One-third
D) The testator's entire estate

Key Takeaway
An unspecified 'share' bequest is interpreted as the smallest heir's share, never less than one-sixth.

Ruling on Bequest of a Part (Juz')
Ruling on bequest of an unspecified part leaving discretion to heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a testator bequeaths an unspecified part (juz') and explain the discretion given to heirs.

Core Idea
A bequest of 'a part' leaves the amount entirely to the heirs' discretion.

In Hanafi law, the wording of a bequest matters. When a testator uses the term 'juz' (part) without specifying the quantity, the ruling is unique: the heirs decide what to give. This lesson explains that ruling and its practical application. The key is that 'juz' is completely ambiguous, so the heirs, standing in the testator's place, have full authority to determine the amount, as long as they give something.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the testator's bequest using the word 'juz'' (part). The ruling is that the heirs are told to give the legatee whatever they wish.
The ruling is obligation (wajib) upon the heirs to give something, but the quantity is at their discretion.
2
Understand the term 'juz''
'Juz'' means an unspecified part; it has no customary minimum. Unlike other terms like 'sahm' (share) which may have a conventional interpretation, 'juz'' is completely open-ended.
This ambiguity is the reason for the heirs' discretion.
3
Note the role of the heirs
After the testator's death, the heirs stand in his place regarding discretionary decisions. They have the authority to determine the amount of the bequest, as long as they give something.
They cannot give nothing; the bequest must be fulfilled, even if by a trivial amount.
4
Distinguish from other bequest terms
Compare 'juz'' with a specified fraction like 'one-third' or with 'sahm'. In the latter cases, the amount is fixed or has a customary interpretation, so heirs have no discretion.
This distinction is important for proper fatwa application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اوطى بجزء من ماله قيل للورثة اعطوه ما شاءوا
And if he bequeaths a part (juz') of his property, the heirs are told: give him whatever they wish.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This is a ruling about a completely unspecified bequest using the term 'juz'' (part). Unlike 'sahm' which has a customary meaning, 'juz'' can refer to any portion, even a minimal amount. Therefore, the heirs (who stand in place of the testator after death) are given discretion to determine the amount, as long as it is something. This ruling gives flexibility to the heirs to fulfill the bequest in the least burdensome way. There is no fixed minimum; even a tiny amount qualifies as 'juz'. The ruling is straightforward and leaves the matter to the heirs' judgment.

Key Terms
جزء (juz'): An unspecified part of property, can be any amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths 'a part of my property' without further specification, how much must the heirs give?
A) One-sixth
B) The smallest heir's share
C) Whatever they wish
D) One-third

Key Takeaway
A bequest of 'juz' (part) gives heirs absolute discretion over the amount, provided they give something.

Bequest of an Unspecified Share: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on bequest of a share and its minimum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a testator bequeaths an unspecified share (sahm) and explain the two key restrictions (minimum one-sixth, maximum one-third) using the mursal hadith proofs.

Core Idea
An unspecified bequest of a share gives the legatee the smallest heir's share, but never less than one-sixth.

When a testator leaves a vague bequest of 'a share' (sahm) without specifying a fraction, how do we determine the legatee's portion? The Hanafi school relies on both linguistic custom and judicial precedent to resolve this ambiguity. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its two important safeguards.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and basic ruling
The testator bequeaths a 'share' (سهم) of his wealth without specifying whether it is one-sixth, one-third, etc. The legatee receives the smallest share that any heir would get in the distribution.
This is the default rule: the legatee steps into the shoes of the least-favored heir.
2
Note the two restrictions
First restriction: if that smallest share is less than one-sixth, it is raised to one-sixth. Second restriction: it cannot exceed one-third without the consent of all heirs, since bequests beyond one-third are invalid without permission.
These boundaries protect both the legatee (minimum) and the heirs (maximum).
3
Examine the linguistic proof for one-sixth
The first hadith (mursal) shows that in Arabic usage, the word 'sahm' (share) defaults to one-sixth. 'Adi asked Iyas, who said: 'The share in the speech of the Arabs is one-sixth.'
This sets the floor: even if the smallest heir's share is less, the legatee gets one-sixth.
4
Examine the procedural proof for the method
The second narration from Shuraih illustrates the method: when a testator left an unspecified share, the shares (i.e., the heirs' portions) are raised and the legatee receives a share (the smallest one).
This precedent establishes the procedure of comparing heirs' shares.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(28) ومن اوطی بسهم من ماله فله اخش سهام الورثة الا ان ينقص عن السدس فيتم له السدس. کسی نے وصیت کی اپنے مال کے ایک سہم کا تو اس کے لئے ورثہ کا کمتر حصہ ملے گا مگر یہ کہ چھٹے کم ہو جائے تو اس کے لئے چھٹا پورا کیا جائے گا۔ کسی نے اپنے مال کے ایک سہم کا کسی کے لئے وصیت کی۔ اور یہ متعین نہیں کیا وہ سہام چھٹا ہے یا تہائی ہے تو اس کے ورثہ میں سے جس کو سب سے کم حصہ ملے گا اتنا ہی موصی لہ کو مل جائے گا۔ البتہ دور عایتیں ضروری ہیں۔ ایک تو یہ کہ یہ حصہ چھٹے سے کم نہ ہو، اگر چھٹے سے کم ہو تو پورا کر کے چھٹا حصہ دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اہل عرب جب مطلق سہم بولتے ہیں تو اس سے چھٹا حصہ مراد لیتے ہیں۔ اور دوسری رعایت یہ ہے کہ تہائی سے زیادہ نہ ہو کیونکہ تہائی سے زیادہ ورثہ کی اجازت کے بغیر وصیت جائز نہیں۔ مطلق سہام سے چھٹا حصہ مراد ہے اس کی دلیل بی اثر ہے۔ ان عدیا سأل اياسا فقال السهم في كلام العرب السدس، دوسرى روایت میں ہے۔ عن شریح انه قضى في رجل اوصى لرجل بسهم من ماله ولم يسم قال ترفع السهام فيكون للموصى له سهم. پہلی روایت سے معلوم ہوا کہ سہم کلام عرب میں چھٹے حصے کو کہتے ہیں۔ اور دوسری روایت سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر سہم کی مقدار متعین نہیں کی تو وارثین میں سے کم حصہ جس کو ملے گا وہ حصہ دلوایا جائے گا۔ انت اخس : کمتر۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عطاء نے فرمایا وصیت میں سے جو چاہے تبدیل کرے مگر آزاد کرنے کو (اس کو تبدیل نہیں کر سکتا ) (ب) ایک آدمی نے ایک آدمی کے لئے وصیت کی ایک حصے کا اور وضاحت نہیں کی تو حضرت شریح نے فیصلہ فرمایا کہ سام اٹھائے اور موصی لہ کے لئے ایک حصہ ہوگا۔
Whoever bequeaths a share of his wealth, he gets the lowest of the heirs' shares, unless it falls below a sixth, then a sixth is completed for him. (Urdu explanation): Someone made a bequest of a share of his wealth. So he will get the least share that the heirs receive, except if it becomes less than one-sixth, then one-sixth will be completed for him. Someone made a bequest of a share of his wealth for someone, and he did not specify whether that share is a sixth or a third. So from among his heirs, whoever gets the smallest share, that much will go to the legatee. However, two considerations are necessary. First, that this share should not be less than one-sixth; if it is less than one-sixth, then one-sixth will be given after completion. Because when the Arabs say an absolute share, they mean one-sixth. Second, that it should not exceed one-third, because bequest of more than one-third is not permissible without the heirs' permission. The proof that from an absolute share one-sixth is meant is the athar: 'Adi asked Iyas, and he said: The word 'share' in the speech of the Arabs means one-sixth.' In another narration: 'Shuraih gave a judgment regarding a man who bequeathed a share of his wealth to a man without specifying, he said: The shares are raised, and for the legatee there will be one share.' From the first narration it is understood that 'share' in Arab speech means one-sixth. And from the second narration it is understood that if the amount of the share is not specified, then the share that the least recipient among the heirs receives will be given. 'Akhass' means least. Footnote: (a) Hadrat Ata said: He may change whatever he wishes from his will except freeing (a slave), he cannot change it. (b) A man bequeathed one share to a man without clarification, so Hadrat Shuraih gave a verdict that the shares be raised, and for the legatee there will be one share.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Kitab al-Wasaya. The matn states that if a person bequeaths a 'share' (sahm) of his wealth without specifying, the legatee receives the smallest share among the heirs, but never less than one-sixth. The commentary explains two key restrictions: (1) the share cannot be less than one-sixth because in Arab usage 'sahm' defaults to one-sixth, and (2) it cannot exceed one-third without the heirs' consent, as per the general rule that bequests are limited to one-third of the estate. The proof is given through two athar: the first from 'Adi ibn Hatim asking Iyas about the meaning of 'sahm'—he confirmed it means one-sixth in Arabic. The second is a judgment of Shuraih that when the testator left a share unspecified, the lowest heir's share was given to the legatee. These establish both the linguistic default and the practical method of distribution. The footnote cites the authority of Ata that manumission (itq) cannot be changed in a will, and Shuraih's judgment is repeated. This ruling ensures that the legatee receives a fair but minimal portion, respecting both the testator's intent and the heirs' rights.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): An unspecified share of the estate; in the Arabic usage of this text, it defaults to one-sixth (suds).
اخس (akhass): The least portion; the smallest share among the heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths 'a share' (sahm) of his estate, what is the minimum amount the legatee must receive?
A) One-third
B) One-sixth
C) One-eighth
D) Whatever the heirs decide

Key Takeaway
An unspecified bequest of a share gives the legatee the smallest heir's share, never less than one-sixth and never more than one-third without heirs' consent.
